1935.12.01

He Yingqin Leaves Nanjing for the North; Song Repeatedly Cables the Central Government Seeking Instructions; Shang Zhen Sends a Representative to Beiping to Return the Visit; Tianjin Security Negotiates Corresponding Measures; Beiping Military Affairs Commission Concludes Its Work 1

(Nanjing) He Yingqin, accompanied by his secretary Xie Zhongyuan and several others, took the Jinpu Railway north to Beiping at 7:30 this evening. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The newly appointed Director of the Executive Yuan's Beiping Office, He Yingqin, took the Pingpu Railway to Beiping to assume his post at 7:00 this afternoon. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Minister of Military Affairs He Yingqin, accompanied by his secretary Xie Zhongyuan and several attendants, boarded the Jinpu Railway at 7:30 p.m. on the 30th and headed north. It is reported that he is going to Beiping. (30th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Jinan) Han Fuju telegraphed urging He Yingqin to go north. He is still preparing. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Song Zheyuan again telegraphed the central government today, hoping that the central government would quickly determine effective measures to comfort public opinion. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) There has been no news of Mr. Han or Mr. Shang coming to Beiping. This afternoon, Song sent a telegram to Chairman Chiang, giving a detailed account and hoping for quick instructions so that there would be something to follow. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Song Zheyuan telegraphed Chairman Chiang on the 30th, laying out the situation in North China and requesting the central government to quickly determine effective measures to comfort public opinion and stabilize public sentiment. The original telegram included phrases such as "Zheyuan is in charge of this region and has detailed knowledge; I respectfully telegraph this report." (30th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Beiping) Regarding the situation in North China, the local authorities, feeling extremely pressured in recent days, have repeatedly telegraphed the central government for instructions. The central government sent a telegram to Beiping last night, saying that the capital currently has no concrete plans and still hopes that Beiping can find its own solutions while struggling to maintain the situation. The military and political authorities here believe that the current situation is extremely urgent and that the so-called "struggle to maintain" has reached its highest limit. It is not easy to come up with other plans at this time, so how to resolve the issue remains to be decided by the central government providing appropriate guidance. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Liu Jialuan, Chief of Staff of the Beiping-Tianjin Garrison Headquarters, was ordered by Song Zheyuan the night before last to go to Baoding to visit Shang Zhen, inquire about his health, and welcome Shang to Beiping to discuss important matters. Liu returned to Beiping this afternoon after visiting Shang in Baoding. Fu Liping, Chief of Staff of the 32nd Army, accompanied him. Liu said that he was ordered by Song to go to Baoding to inquire about Shang's health and welcome Shang to Beiping to discuss ways to handle the current situation. After arriving in Baoding, he met with Shang yesterday. As a result, Shang was unable to come north and specially sent Fu, Chief of Staff of the 32nd Army, as his representative to visit Song and ask for instructions on everything. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Cheng Ke returned to Tianjin from Beiping on the evening of the 30th. His old illness relapsed on the way. Upon arriving in Tianjin, he got off the train at the main station. When he returned to his residence, he asked Secretary-General Sun Runyu and Public Security Bureau Chief Liu Yushu to visit him, but he was unable to speak. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Cheng Ke came to Beiping a few days ago to visit Song Zheyuan and discuss the issue of security in Tianjin. The result was satisfactory. Song agreed to take responsibility for maintaining it. Cheng left Beiping this afternoon to return to Tianjin. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Cheng Ke told people on the 30th that he had met Song Zheyuan several times in Beiping and had negotiated corresponding measures for the security of Tianjin. He hoped that citizens would not disturb themselves. (30th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Beiping) The Military Affairs Commission was basically concluded on the 30th and will cease operations from the 1st. Documents and equipment will be temporarily kept in Beiping, awaiting the Military Affairs Commission to send personnel to take over. (30th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Zhu Shiqin and He Qigong arrived in Tianjin from Beiping at around 5:00 p.m. on the 30th. (30th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Cao Kun, Wang Yitang, and Qi Xieyuan have no intention of going to Beiping. However, a certain party did seek opinions on the new organization in North China. Cao and Qi made no indication, and Wang's reply was also ambiguous. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) The Beiping Military Affairs Commission concluded everything today in accordance with Nanjing's instructions. The matters previously handled by the Military Affairs Commission will henceforth be handled by the Nanjing Military Affairs Commission. It is reported that Chinese leaders here held a secret meeting last night and did not disperse until 4:00 today. When the meeting dispersed, an important telegram was sent to Nanjing, requesting more concrete instructions. It is reported that this telegram was addressed to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, Minister of Finance Kung, and Minister of Military Affairs He. It was rumored that Doihara originally planned to leave Beiping today, but he is still staying here, probably for another two or three days. The Beiping Labor Union and the Hebei Provincial Farmers' Association both telegraphed the central government today, expressing their loyalty, denouncing the puppet organization calling itself the Hebei East Autonomous Council, and declaring that they would never cooperate with it. (30th Reuters Dispatch)

Ambassador Shi Visits the U.S. Secretary of State; The U.S. Opposes the Separatist Movement in North China 2

(Washington) Secretary of State Hull met with Chinese Ambassador to the United States Shi Zhaoji today to discuss the situation in North China. Both sides remained silent about the content of the conversation. (29th Kuomin News)

(Washington) Official circles here indicated today that although they have not formally inquired about Japan's true intentions regarding the situation in North China from Tokyo, the U.S. government has sufficient information. This statement was in response to newspaper reports on whether the United States would follow Britain and take the same action towards Japan. Officials here declined to comment on future actions but said that they have not yet conducted this inquiry. The State Department's attitude is to avoid directly opposing Japan before the reaction in China is clear. However, the United States has always upheld the Nine-Power Treaty and, in principle, strongly opposes the separatist movement in North China. (29th Kuomin News)

(London) It was learned today that when Britain inquired about Japan's intentions in North China, it did not directly invoke the Nine-Power Treaty. However, it has been confirmed that Britain formally requested Japan to explain its intentions regarding the autonomous movement in North China. This matter was inquired about by Zhang Jing, the British Chargé d'Affaires in Tokyo, to Shigemitsu, the Vice Minister of the Japanese Foreign Ministry, with the aim of clarifying the truth in order to have a basis for Britain to invoke the Nine-Power Treaty in the future. (29th Kuomin News Agency Dispatch)

British and American Ambassadors Visited Qin Dechun Yesterday; Counselors from the American and German Embassies Visited Vice Foreign Minister Xu 3

(Beiping) British and American Ambassadors Knatchbull-Hugessen and Grew visited Qin Dechun separately this morning to inquire about the flood situation in our country. City government commissioner Wang Zengsi translated. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Counselor and Consul-General of the U.S. Embassy in Nanjing, Peck, visited Vice Foreign Minister Xu Mo at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs at 3:30 p.m. on the 30th to inquire about Sino-American diplomatic incidents and the situation in Hebei. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Counselor Fischer of the German Embassy visited Vice Minister Xu at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs at 4:00 p.m. on the 30th and stated that the note regarding all acts of the rebellious Yin (Rugen) being considered invalid by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs had been telegraphed to his home government for reporting and inquired about the current situation in Hebei. (30th Special Dispatch)

Wang Zhengting Arrives in Tokyo 4

Yokohama - Mr. Wang Zhengting arrived in Yokohama at 6:00 a.m. on the 30th. He told reporters that he had passed through Japan by car during the Great Kanto Earthquake seventeen years ago. This time, he came to Japan to see the current situation in Japan. He plans to stay in Japan for about ten days and intends to meet with Foreign Minister Hirota and other important figures to exchange views. Wang did not touch on political issues in his speech. After the speech, he went to the embassy in Tokyo with Counselor Ding Shaoji. (30th Combined Dispatch)

Commanders of Two Japanese Warships Arrived in Tianjin Yesterday to Meet Tada 5

(Tianjin) Lieutenant Commander Suetsugu Hisamunejiro, commander of the 14th Japanese Destroyer Squadron, and Major Kunitoshi Takeharu, commander of the Kikukaze, were invited to Tianjin by Tada on the 30th and consulted on measures to protect overseas Chinese in the emergency period at the Commander's residence in Zhang Garden. (30th Special Dispatch)

Rumors Abound in Baoding; Local Security is Tight 6

(Tianjin) Rumors abound in the Baoding telephone, government, and business circles, and merchants are panicking. The authorities fear that criminals will take the opportunity to cause trouble and have specially transferred the guard regiment of the 32nd Army and the provincial government duty team to jointly deploy defenses. The Public Security Bureau has also formed a bicycle team to patrol. (30th Special Dispatch)

The Situation in Various Counties in the War Zone is Chaotic; Yin Rugeng Remains in Tong County and Has Not Gone Elsewhere; The Pseudo-Supervisory Office of the Xin-Yu Section Sends Commissioners and Section Chiefs; More Than Ten Counties, Including Changping, Declare That They Will Not Betray; Various Groups Urgently Request the Central Government to Clearly Order the Suppression of the Rebels 7

(Tianjin) Since the declaration of pseudo-autonomy in the war zone, people have been uneasy and have fled to Beiping, Tianjin, and the mining bureau to seek refuge. Poor people have dug cellars in their houses to prevent any eventuality. Stores are panicked and close early every day. Gunshots are heard every night in Tangshan, and hooligans are active everywhere, taking the opportunity to rob. Those who know the ronin are seeking official positions. Commercial companies and institutions with the words "Central" in their names on the streets are forced to change their names. Japanese planes fly over every morning and are forbidden to fly the national flag. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) The pseudo-autonomous association of Hebei East in Tong County has been extremely busy working for several days. Yin Rugeng is still staying in Tong County, receiving guests every day and has not gone elsewhere. The Tangshan Hebei East Anti-Communist Association Office has been intercepting tax funds. Each tax bureau has separately telegraphed the competent authority to ask for instructions. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) The Kanto Army Air Force has allocated one aircraft to the Hebei East Anti-Communist Autonomous Committee, named "Hebei East" and said to be purchased by 22 counties, intending to use it for reconnaissance in our inland areas to avoid the Japanese side directly invading our airspace. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) The Xin-Yu Section of the Hebei East Railway Supervisory Office is divided into six sections internally: General Affairs, Accounting, Transportation, Engineering, Machinery, and Police. On the 29th, the office announced that Bo Zhu was the chief of the General Affairs Section, Han Zikui was the chief of the Accounting Section, Chen Juesheng, director of the Tangshan Transportation Section, was the chief of the Transportation Section, Xie Zhen, director of the Tangshan Railway Factory, was the chief of the Machinery Section, Xu Kaixian, engineer of the Tangshan Taxation Project, was the chief of the Engineering Section, and Qu Shihe was the chief of the Police Section. The letters of appointment have been issued, but the original on-duty employees of the Beining Railway, although they have received the letters of appointment, have not worked for them. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) The director of the pseudo-supervisory office, Lu Qiu, went to Beiping, but his whereabouts have been unknown for days. Some say that he has broken away from the pseudo-organization and secretly went south from Beiping to report to the central government. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) The train service at each station east of Xinhe on the Beining Railway on the 30th was normal. Although the pseudo-supervisory office has been organized, it has not yet taken over the road affairs. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Shang Zhen, chairman of the Hebei Provincial Government, telegraphed to report that the county chiefs in the Ping-Ji area, since Yin's rebellion, either sent written reports or sent personnel to the government, declaring that they would never betray. Currently, there are more than ten counties, including Changping, Xianghe, Yutian, Ninghe, Shunyi, Sanhe, Pinggu, Leting, Linyu, Funing, and Lulong. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Since Yin declared his rebellion, the Ministry of Finance telegraphed the Tianjin Unified Tax Inspection Office to instruct the on-site tax collection personnel to stop paying taxes on-site and switch to collecting at the first checkpoint after shipping. The personnel have agreed to comply with the order after receiving it. The Inspection Office telegraphed the Ministry of Finance on the 30th, saying that some tax collection personnel have not returned because they received the order later. As for the Kailuan Mining Bureau, due to its foreign relations, it has decided not to pay money to the pseudo-collection bureau. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Yin Rugeng's younger brother, Yin Tixin, formed the Tangshan Office of the Hebei East Anti-Communist Autonomous Committee in Tangshan, divided into three sections. Wu Daquan has been appointed as the chief of the first section, Zhang Qingcheng as the chief of the second section, and the chief of the third section has not yet been determined. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) The pseudo Xin-Yu section of the Supervisory Office estimates that the income of this section of the railway will be 700,000 per month. After deducting 400,000 in expenses, the surplus will be about 300,000. However, the Kailuan coal transportation fee has always been recorded on account, totaling 300,000, so there is actually no surplus. Wang Xiacai, director of the Construction Department of the Pseudo Hebei East Committee, went to Linyu on the 30th to promote the meaning of autonomy. On the way back, he went to various stations to investigate and convened a meeting of county chiefs in Tangshan on behalf of Yin Rugeng. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) According to the Tongzhou telephone, the 22 counties under the pseudo-organization jointly purchased an aircraft, named it "Hebei East," and presented it to the pseudo-organization. It is scheduled to fly around the sky tomorrow and distribute propaganda. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Due to the recent heavy traffic on the Beining Railway Bureau, it issued a notice to all stations along the line yesterday, urging them to pay attention to the safe operation of trains and the proper handling of temporary accidents. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Academic groups in the capital city, in response to Yin's rebellion, telegraphed Song and Shang to eliminate traitors and defend against insults, and resolved: 1. Issue a declaration requesting that Yin and his family be severely punished and their property confiscated. Request the government to make a final decision to maintain the integrity of territory and sovereignty with strength. Demand the opening of freedom of speech, assembly, association, and publication to awaken the national people to support the government as the government's backing. 2. Request the Legislative Yuan to formulate special regulations for punishing traitors. 3. Contact academic groups in the capital city to form a joint association of academic groups in the capital city and scheduled to convene an establishment meeting on the 4th. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Jiangsu Provincial Middle School Joint Association recently telegraphed Song Zheyuan, Shang Zhen, and Han Fuju, requesting that they suppress the rebels and eliminate traitors to seek the integrity of the country's territory. (30th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The presidents of middle schools in the capital jointly telegraphed Song Zheyuan and Shang Zhen, requesting that they be responsible for defending the territory and eliminating the rebels. (30th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Chinese Education Society, in response to Yin's rebellion and disruption of the country, recently telegraphed Director Song of the Ping-Sui Pacification Headquarters and Chairman Shang of Baoding, requesting that they eliminate the rebels to quell the chaos in the country. (30th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The faculty and staff of National Central University and Jinling University previously telegraphed Shang Zhen to condemn the rebels. Yesterday, they received Shang's reply telegram, which read: (Omitted) "I have received the telegram. The country is in peril, traitors are rampant, and we are all deeply indignant. I, Zhen, with my meager talents, have been entrusted with the responsibility of defending the territory and eliminating traitors. I will not hesitate to do so. I am grateful for your encouragement. I am sincerely yours, Shang Zhen." (30th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Ma Lisan and other overseas representatives of the Fifth National Congress telegraphed Song Zheyuan, Director of the Ji-Cha-Sui Pacification Headquarters, on the 29th, hoping that he would use his past spirit of defending the country to eliminate the evildoers and pacify the locality. (30th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Fellow villagers from the eight counties of Xuzhou in Nanjing issued a public telegram on the 30th denouncing Yin's rebellion, requesting that the central government immediately suppress it to secure North China. (30th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanchang) The Jiangxi Student Autonomous Association and various youth service groups telegraphed the central government, clearly ordering the suppression of Yin's rebellion, and telegraphed Song, Xiao, etc. to suppress the rebellion and secure the territory. (30th Special)

(Nanchang) Academic groups in this city telegraphed the central government and Song Zheyuan, clearly ordering the suppression of the rebel Yin Rugeng. (30th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Jiangning County Farmers' Association telegraphed the central government and Song and Shang, requesting that Yin's rebellion be suppressed. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Guiyang) Various civil groups in this city, feeling that the national crisis is the most serious, convened a meeting yesterday and passed a resolution to telegraph the central government, quickly deciding on a plan to save the country, and telegraphed Shang Zhen, Song Zheyuan, Qin Dechun, etc., requesting that they seek survival for the nation. This afternoon, they also sent representatives to visit Liu Jimin, the chief of staff of the Pacification Headquarters, asking him to step up the work of suppressing bandits. (30th Central News Agency Dispatch)

The Air Defense Drill in Nanjing and Hangzhou is Completed; Results Have Improved Compared to Last Year 8

(Nanjing) The Nanjing-Hangzhou joint air defense drill was the third day on the 30th. In the morning, hypothetical enemy planes launched a large-scale attack from Hangzhou, simulating aerial and ground combat, as well as various passive air defense actions and security duties. More than 10,000 people were mobilized in a light breeze and drizzle to practice various actions, which were realistic and the results were satisfactory. In the afternoon, due to bad weather, the scheduled procedures were stopped, and this year's joint air defense exercise was completed. In the morning of the 30th, all the officers of the Air Defense Headquarters gathered to quietly await reports from surveillance posts in various places. At 8:58, enemy planes attacked the capital from a certain direction, and the Air Defense Department issued an air raid alarm at 9:00, starting traffic control. At 9:30, an emergency alarm was issued, and traffic was completely stopped. When the air raid alarm started, the smoke screen brigade immediately released smoke screens at the National Government, gradually increasing the equipment, the smoke screen was thicker, and pedestrians could not be seen two feet away until the alarm was lifted and stopped. When enemy planes flew to the capital, they dropped incendiary bombs in places such as Central Road, and the fire quickly obscured the sky. The entire fire brigade rushed to various places and extinguished the fire within a few minutes. The enemy planes also used explosive bombs to damage water pipes and telephone lines, which were repaired by the engineering team. The enemy planes also dropped poison gas bombs, and the anti-poisoning and rescue teams stepped up their work, treating the wounded and disinfecting the area. Thousands of people from the rescue brigade were dispatched at the same time to practice rescue work on important streets, which was extremely rapid and orderly. When enemy planes dropped bombs in various places, various anti-aircraft weapons fired at the same time, and the sound of cannons shook the sky. The enemy planes were finally forced back. At 10:10, the capital was no longer threatened by enemy planes, and the headquarters issued an order to lift the alarm, traffic was restored, and the personnel of each team returned to their teams. The capital was restored to its original state. The Air Defense Department held a lecture at Lishi Society at 3:30 pm on the 30th. Several hundred officers of various departments attended. First, Commander-in-Chief Tang Shengzhi gave a lecture, saying that the results of this exercise were better than last year. The weather had been bad for several days, but the troops, especially the air force, were still able to complete the exercise according to the scheduled procedures, which was admirable. The efforts of the boy scouts and male and female students to participate were also commendable. However, traffic and light control have not yet reached the ideal state and should be improved. Next, Commander Yang Jie, Deputy Commander Huang Zhenqiu, and advisors made speeches. It was not until 5 o'clock that they dispersed. (30th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Hangzhou) The Hangzhou air defense drill was the third day on the 30th. From 8:00 a.m. to 10:00 a.m., middle schools and above in the city formed protection groups to practice. (30th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Japanese Troops in Tianjin Build an Airfield, Occupying a Lot of Farmland; Japanese Planes Reconnoiter the Great Wall Area 9

(Tianjin) The area of the airfield built by the Japanese in Judzsuo in eastern Tianjin has been expanded to the north of the International Racecourse, occupying a total of more than 3,000 mu. In addition to the land of the Beining, the rest is farmland. On the 30th, two thatched sheds were built in the field for workers to rest. Chen Dongsheng, a member of the Hebei Provincial Government, visited Japanese Consul General Kawagoe again on the 30th to negotiate, but there was no result. Local households have complained to the Tianjin County Government, demanding the return of the land. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) It is widely rumored in Tangshan that the large training ground at the station will be converted into an airfield. Someone brought instruments here this morning to measure. It is said that construction will begin in December. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) According to the Tangshan telephone, Japanese reconnaissance planes flew over Tangshan from the east both yesterday and this morning to reconnoiter. Yesterday, a Japanese reconnaissance plane flew and landed at the Tangshan Station training ground. It is said that it was to convey a message and then flew towards Yuguan. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) According to the report from the war zone, the Japanese military airfield in Malanyu has been concentrated for days. Five or six Japanese planes fly to various counties near the Great Wall every day to reconnoiter. The Japanese military is extremely busy with troop movements, but the order in each county is peaceful. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) A Japanese plane flew from eastern Tianjin in the morning, circling in the sky, and then landed at the Balitai airfield. At midday, it flew back to Guanwai. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) On the morning of the 30th, a Japanese plane flew from Guanwai and landed at the Balitai airfield. A senior officer of the Kwantung Army arrived, said to be Vice Chief of Staff Itagaki. After meeting with Tada at noon, he flew back to Guanwai. (30th Special Dispatch)

Japanese Soldiers in Fengtai Continue to Monitor Vehicles 10

(Beiping) Several Japanese soldiers in Fengtai are still monitoring vehicles very strictly. All road freight is not allowed to cross the tracks. Passenger cars heading south are allowed to pass as usual after inspection. The Beining Railway Bureau issued a notice to all stations on the 30th, urging them to pay special attention to the safety of trains and freight along the line and not to be negligent. (30th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) According to sources in the transportation sector, Japanese troops in Tianjin Main Station and Fengtai had not withdrawn on the 30th. The numbers of each passenger and freight train heading south are recorded one by one for verification when they return north, but the trains have not been obstructed. (30th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Japanese Troops are Continuously Transported South from Guanwai; Waiting for the Opportunity to Enter Beiping and Tianjin 11

(Tianjin) About a brigade of Japanese troops in the Xinmingou-Bangzi area boarded eight trains of the pseudo Fengshan Railway at 2:00 a.m. and arrived at QianSuo outside Guanwai, only two stations away from Shanhaiguan. Most of the Japanese troops, about nine trains, arrived again on the night of the 30th. The Oritaka Brigade of the Kwantung Army, which is attacking the Volunteer Army in the Jilin-Changchun area, is gathering at Jinxi and Suizhong outside Guanwai, waiting for the opportunity to enter Beiping and Tianjin. The Kwantung Army has decided to transfer one brigade from the 4th Division, currently stationed in Northeast China, and one brigade from the 1st Division into Guan, together with the North China Garrison Army, totaling 18,000 troops. The newly arrived Japanese troops are all carrying chemical warfare equipment. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) According to the Miyun telephone, Kawagishi, the commander of the Independent Mixed Brigade of the Kwantung Army stationed in Jehol, arrived at Gubeikou by plane from Chengde this morning. Major Ishii and others welcomed him. After getting off the plane, Kawagishi went to the Hexi Headquarters to rest. Kawagishi came to Gubei to inspect the local situation and review the recently arrived troops under his command. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) According to the Miyun telephone, more than 20 officers and 20 soldiers of the Japanese Kawagishi troops who arrived at Gubeikou, fully armed, took two cars and arrived in Miyun from Gubeikou this morning to inspect. They left Miyun at noon to the south and arrived in Huairou at 1:00 p.m. They then went to Niulanshan and other places to inspect and returned to Gubeikou that day. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Tō Kyō, staff officer of the Tianjin Japanese Army, and Major Hayashi, accompanied by Liu Yushu, director of the Public Security Bureau, went to the former site of the 51st Army's Rear Hospital in Hebei and the site of the Qingfeng Flour Company on the afternoon of the 30th to survey and decided to use them as barracks for the troops arriving from Yuguan. (30th Special Dispatch)

Strict Prohibition of Spreading Rumors in Tangshan 12

(Beiping) Rumors have been rampant in Tangshan recently, causing unease. At the same time, bandits have sneaked in, resulting in frequent robbery and kidnapping cases. Gunshots are heard every night, and people are startled several times a night. Zhao Lei, commander of the Fourth Security Brigade, issued a notice on the 29th to reassure the people and strictly prohibit the spreading of rumors. (30th Special Dispatch)

The Chairman of the First Plenary Session is Temporarily Appointed 13

(Nanjing) The First Plenary Session is scheduled to open at 9:00 a.m. on the 2nd. According to precedent, the temporary chairmen of the opening ceremony and preparatory meeting of the Plenary Session are appointed by the Standing Committee. However, the Fifth Standing Committee has not yet been formed. Therefore, the temporary chairman this time will be temporarily appointed at the opening ceremony and will serve as the chairman of the Plenary Session and swear in the Central Executive Committee members and supervisors when they take office. (30th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) For the Fifth Plenary Session, the Chairman of the National Government, members of the National Government, and the heads of the Five Yuan should resign from their positions to the Central Government as usual. Whether to reappoint them will be decided by the Plenary Session. During the period of routine resignation, they will continue to be responsible for the affairs of the Yuan. Other officials appointed by the National Government will not need to resign. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) According to the Executive Yuan, the Fifth Plenary Session will open on the 2nd. At that time, the candidates for the heads of the Five Yuan will be reappointed in accordance with the law. President Wang Zhaoming must submit his resignation in accordance with the organizational law and has submitted his resignation to the Central Government and resigned from his concurrent position as Minister of Foreign Affairs. (30th Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Liu Jiwen, Lin Yunkai, Huang Jilu, and Wang Luyi arrived in the capital from Shanghai on the evening of the 30th to attend the First Plenary Session on the 2nd. (30th Special Dispatch)

Current Affairs Commentary

The Understanding That Chinese People Should Have Regarding the North China Situation 14

—Advocacy

Since the Tongzhou Incident occurred, Sino-Japanese relations have become increasingly strained. The Japanese army has increased its troops in eastern Hebei and once occupied important stations between Beiping and Tianjin. They have used every possible means of coercion. The National Government has also failed to effectively address the puppet autonomous movement of the Yin Rugeng clique. At this moment, when the provinces of North China are once again in a state of unrest, all Chinese people with a sense of national consciousness should deeply feel their responsibility to save the nation. However, when we talk about saving the nation today, we must first have a clear understanding of the current North China situation. Let us discuss this from three aspects.

First, under the current circumstances, Japan does have intentions to deeply penetrate North China. However, its government, considering the attitudes of Britain and the United States and the national sentiment of our people, still has to take some concerns into account. Seizing North China by force is definitely not what they want. After all, what benefit would it be to Japan if North China became a scorched earth? However, Japanese militarists may still want to emulate the Shenyang Incident and create a new situation in North China through independent actions, waiting for their government to endorse it. The puppet autonomous organizations in eastern Hebei are one example. But we must know that although the arrogance of the Japanese militarists is strong, if our entire nation unites and responds with a firm will and prudent attitude, then their temporary arrogance can be slightly contained.

Second, North China generals such as Song Zheyuan, Shang Zhen, and Han Fuju, judging from their past attitudes, are all capable of deeply understanding righteousness and being loyal to the central government. Recently, they have resisted threats and inducements and have not plunged into the vortex of puppet autonomy, which further demonstrates their upright integrity. The people of the country should give the generals of North China great trust and encouragement, so that they can fulfill their responsibilities of defending their territory.

Third, our government's diplomatic policy towards Japan has been clearly expressed by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek in his speech at the Fifth Plenary Session of the National Congress. To summarize, it is "to seek political coordination with friendly nations within the limit of not infringing upon sovereignty" and "to be determined for the final sacrifice and to make the greatest efforts for peace." Recently, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has lodged serious protests with the Japanese Ambassador to China regarding the so-called "North China Autonomous Movement" instigated by Japanese militarists in China and the Japanese army's unauthorized occupation of Fengtai Railway Station. It has also notified all countries that Yin Rugeng's treasonous acts are invalid. The newly appointed Director of the Executive Yuan's Beiping Office, He Yingqin, also set off north yesterday to deal with everything. All of this proves that our government is strictly adhering to the maximum limit of tolerance and making the greatest efforts for peace. The timeliness of this diplomatic action is something that the people of the country should recognize.

Although the situation in North China today is extremely serious, it has not yet reached the point of hopelessness for peace. The people of the country should use calm and meticulous minds to carefully consider the future of the nation and use the united will of the whole country to provide a strong backing for the government's diplomacy. If there is no mutual trust and understanding within the country, and people are still acting impulsively and recklessly to seek temporary gratification, then the future of our nation will be unimaginable.

Exhibition of Chinese Antiquities in London

First Day Sees Over Three Thousand Visitors; Various European Languages Can Be Heard; Experts and Journalists Specially Sent by Various Countries to Write Reports; Parisian Clothing Stores Adopt Chinese-Style Colors; The British Emperor and Empress, Along with the Royal Family, Also Visit 15

(London) The British Emperor will visit the Chinese art exhibition with the Empress, the Duke and Duchess of Kent, and other members of the royal family on Sunday. Judging from the current situation, the exhibition will be an unprecedented success. Yesterday was the first day open to the public, and there were over three thousand visitors, more than a thousand more than on the opening day of the British art exhibition. The art exhibitions held in London in the past have never had as many visitors as yesterday. There are still many visitors today. Admission is five shillings per person. According to a doorman, "I have never seen so many visitors to an art exhibition. It is truly rare." At the entrance of the exhibition hall, there are two beautiful Chinese girls dressed in red Chinese silk clothing, helping to sell photos of the exhibits. The number of foreigners visiting the exhibition is particularly astonishing. Various European languages can be heard in the exhibition hall. About forty people are recognized as experts in Chinese art, specially sent by major European newspapers to report on the exhibition. Germany alone has four people. They have already arrived one after another. A famous clothing store in Paris has adopted Chinese-style colors and styles, creating many new clothes. Literary, cultural, and commercial groups from all over Europe send letters to Burlington House every day inquiring about convenient travel arrangements to visit the exhibition in England. The British textile industry is now paying close attention to the exhibition. The Bradford Chamber of Commerce has specially sent several experts to visit and study everything. After receiving their reports, the chairman and all directors plan to come and feast their eyes on the exhibition in person. Dr. David is scheduled to begin giving sixteen lectures on Chinese art today, presided over by Prince Adolph of Sweden, an art expert. This is organized by the Royal Society, whose building is adjacent to Burlington House. The number of tickets purchased exceeds the capacity of the venue by three times. Six lectures have already been sold out. Many visitors spend half a day focusing on one exhibit, indicating that they will come back to see the other exhibits in the future. Today, the room of ancient bronze artifacts from the Shang and Zhou dynasties is attracting the most attention. Visitors are amazed by its beauty. (Reuters, 29th)

Sven Hedin Discovers Ten Thousand Pieces of Chinese Wood Carvings 16

(Berlin) The famous Swedish explorer Dr. Sven Hedin has conducted surveys in Central Asia, West Asia, and Chinese Xinjiang and Mongolia for many years. He recently gave a lecture here entitled "Eight Years of Struggle in Central Asia and West Asia." He claimed to have discovered about ten thousand pieces of Chinese wood carvings, with ancient writing on them. He is currently working on translating them, which will take about ten years to complete. It is hoped that a true picture of ancient Chinese life two thousand years ago can be obtained through this. (Havas, 30th)

Japanese Ships Navigate the Heilongjiang River; Soviet Union Protests to Japan; Foreign Minister Hirota Promises to Investigate the Situation 17

(Moscow) The Soviet Ambassador to Japan, Yurenev, protested to Japanese Foreign Minister Hirota as follows: "According to the Treaty of Aigun of 1858, only ships of the Qing Dynasty and Russia are allowed to navigate the Heilongjiang River, the Songhua River, and the Ussuri River. Furthermore, according to the agreement signed in 1934 between the Heilongjiang State-Run Shipping Company and the Harbin Water Transport Bureau of Manchukuo, only ships of Manchukuo and the Soviet Union are allowed to pass through the aforementioned rivers. However, on October 29th, a ship flying the Japanese flag left the mouth of the Songhua River and sailed down the Heilongjiang River. Ships flying the Japanese flag have previously attempted to enter the Heilongjiang River and the Songhua River." Yurenev pointed out that the illegal entry of Japanese ships into the Heilongjiang River and the Ussuri River violates the treaty. Therefore, he asked Hirota to investigate this matter thoroughly and take measures to ensure that similar actions do not occur in the future. Hirota replied that he had not heard of the matters listed by Yurenev and promised to investigate the situation. (TASS, 30th)

Among them, the military budget is 500 million yen for the Army and 550 million yen for the Navy, totaling 1,050 million yen, accounting for 46.3% of the total expenditure. The Army held a leadership meeting regarding the Ministry of Finance's budget proposal and made another revival request. As a result, the Ministry of Finance has reached a compromise with the Army in yesterday's cabinet meeting, approving the Army's revival request of 8 million yen and the Navy's revival request of 2 million yen. The difficult hurdle of Japan's budget issue has been overcome. (Hualian, 20th)

Japanese Budget Compromise; Military Dissatisfied with Minister of the Army; Financial Circles Consider it Gratifying 19

(Tokyo) The budget cabinet felt great difficulty in breaking through the difficult hurdle of the military budget. A compromise was reached only this morning. The final budget cabinet meeting was held from 7:10 AM, where Finance Minister Takahashi presented his views, stating that compared to the original assessment of the Ministry of Finance, the first approval of 10 million yen each for the Army and Navy, and the second approval of 8 million yen for the Army and 2 million yen for the Navy for revival requests, but that the financial resources were not sought from public bonds, which was in line with his intentions. Minister of the Army Kawashima then expressed his gratitude for the lengthy budget process. The extremely dangerous cabinet meeting at one time dissipated, and all cabinet members were delighted. The meeting adjourned at 7:20 AM. (Dentsu, 30th)

(Tokyo) After the government budget was decided, Prime Minister Okada issued a statement saying, "It is gratifying that the budget for 1936 was successfully decided with the enthusiasm and cooperation of all cabinet members. The current domestic and international situation is serious, and national defense must be emphasized, while industry and other aspects must also be emphasized. Compiling the budget was very difficult, but it was resolved with the spirit of mutual cooperation among the ministries." Minister of the Army Kawashima also said that the total budget for the Army is 508 million yen. The focus of the discussion last night was on the equipment preparation costs. As a result, it was decided that 400 million yen would be allocated for six years, and 55 million yen would be allocated for the first year (i.e., 1936). The equipment preparation plan mainly focuses on preparing aircraft, which is absolutely necessary for the current war plan. From the perspective of the General Staff Headquarters, this amount is not satisfactory. However, considering the current financial situation, this amount had to be decided. (Nichiren, 30th)

(Tokyo) Minister of the Navy Osumi said, "The budget has been decided, which is very gratifying. However, the Navy's budget is over 550 million yen, which is the minimum from the perspective of military reduction. The Navy will also not neglect domestic issues that must be urgently addressed, such as cultivating national strength, revitalizing rural areas, and recovering from disasters. The belief that solid military strength must be built on a solid foundation of national power will not waver. When exercising this budget, we should strive for the best economy and efficiency to achieve economic military preparedness and prevent the outflow of excessive national funds overseas, in order to contribute to the development of local people's strength." (Dentsu, 30th)

(Tokyo) Although the Army's financial authorities have reached a compromise and the compromise of 8 million yen has been allocated, there is suspicion of disregarding the operational stance of the General Staff Headquarters. Within the Army, the theory of responsibility of Minister of the Army Kawashima has gradually emerged. (Dentsu, 30th)

(Tokyo) The leaders of the General Staff Headquarters oppose Minister of the Army Kawashima's compromise on the Army budget in both substance and spirit. However, since the Minister of the Army has already expressed his approval in the cabinet meeting, superficially opposing it would expose the issue of the Army's dignity. Therefore, they reluctantly accepted the compromise. Moreover, for this reason, the breakdown of the cabinet meeting was avoided. The General Staff Headquarters' approval is superficial, and inwardly, there is concern that the compromise will make it difficult to maintain the military strength that is the fundamental element for breaking through the extraordinary situation. Furthermore, the fact that the post and telecommunications employees' treatment expenses were obtained has left a deep impression on the people, which has led to dissatisfaction. The same opinion is held within the Ministry of the Army. Therefore, Minister of the Army Kawashima's position has become delicate, and its progress is noteworthy. In particular, the problematic issue is that 3 million yen of the revived 8 million yen is incorporated into a special account, and most of this account is closely related to the mass life of proletarian employees within the scope of the special account. Therefore, using it to strengthen the core of breaking through the extraordinary situation is inconsistent with the spirit of the Imperial Army and goes against the Army's long-promoted broad national defense policy. Therefore, the strong argument is that even if shortcomings are tolerable, from the perspective of the spirit of the Imperial Army and the spirit of Japan, the 3 million yen should be returned to the Ministry of Finance. Therefore, its future is noteworthy. (Dentsu, 30th)

(Tokyo) Governor Fukai of the Bank of Japan made the following remarks regarding the successful formulation of the budget proposal: "From the perspective of the Bank of Japan, I would like to avoid criticizing the content of the budget. However, it is gratifying that the iron rule of gradually reducing public bonds has been implemented, which is beneficial in terms of digesting public bonds and maintaining credit. Each aspect may view it with goodwill. Japan's deficit public bonds have now reached a considerable amount, but without adverse effects, which is considered incredible by all countries. Therefore, the current budget formulation will have a better impact on foreign credit." (Dentsu, 30th)

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Justice believes that the cases of killing relatives reported by various courts are often excessively lenient, which is a misunderstanding of the legislative intent of Article 272 of the new criminal law. On the 30th, it issued a special circular to all courts, stating that in the future, when handling major cases of killing relatives, the personnel involved must carefully investigate and prudently handle the matter, and must not misunderstand the legislative intent and give a general lighter sentence with sweeping language. If the most severe sentence is improperly applied to such cases, or if it is known to be improper and no appeal is filed, disciplinary action will be taken upon discovery to maintain social morality and promote fundamental solutions. Japanese Cabinet Negotiates All Night to Compile a Budget Compromise; Approval of 10 Million Yen Additional Funding for the Army; Total Amount is 2.27 Billion Yen; Shortage of Over 1 Million Yen, But No Public Bonds Issued 40

(Tokyo) The Government Budget Cabinet continued to meet on the morning and afternoon of the 29th. Regulations of the Executive Yuan of Our Nation Regarding Sanctions Against Italy: Order to Comply in Both Substance and Finance 41

(Nanjing) Regarding the League of Nations' sanctions against Italy, suggestions three and four, our Executive Yuan has stipulated the following implementation measures: (1) The following items are prohibited from being exported to Italy and its territories from December 1st: (A) Mules, donkeys, camels, and various transportation animals; (B) Rubber; (C) Alum, alumina, iron seedlings, and scrap iron, manganese, nickel, titanium, tungsten, vanadium, and their ores, as well as iron alloys, plow steel, high-silicon steel, manganese steel, manganese-silicon-aluminum steel, tin, and their ores. The above items include all unrefined minerals and metal ore fragments and alloys. (2) From December 1st, no more commercial contracts may be entered into with any Italian groups, companies, or individuals regarding the import of Italian goods into China. (3) Purchase contracts for which payment has not been made before December g date should be canceled immediately. (4) Purchase contracts for which payment has been made in full or more than 20% before December 1st are exempt from cancellation. (5) Italian goods imported into China that are already en route are exempt from import prohibition, but only those entering the country before January 1st, 1936, are exempt; imports after this date are prohibited. (6) Goods produced in Italy or its territories that have undergone a transformation process in other countries, as well as goods partially manufactured in Italy or its territories and partially manufactured in other countries, shall also be prohibited from import if imported after January 1st, 1936. However, if 25% or more of the value of the goods when exported from the final location is due to a certain transformation process, and this process is carried out after the goods leave Italy or its territories, they are exempt from prohibition. (7) The following items are not prohibited from import even if imported after January 1st, 1936: (A) Gold and silver bullion coins; (B) Books, newspapers, magazines, and maps; (C) Nautical charts, printed materials, printing plates, and music; (D) Personal belongings carried by travelers. (8) Goods that violate the ban, whether imported or exported, shall be treated as smuggled goods and handled in accordance with the Customs Anti-Smuggling Regulations. Regarding the contractual matters in the above measures, the Ministry of Industry will order local chambers of commerce to instruct all merchants and commercial organizations to comply. Regarding the ban on the import and export of goods, the Ministry of Finance will order all customs offices to comply. (Central News Agency dispatch, 30th)

Italian Army Faces Difficulties in Attacking Egypt: Five Impossibilities 43

Alexandria According to a Reuters correspondent in the Suez Canal area, no one is paying attention to the talk of an Italian invasion of Egypt, no matter how many troops Mussolini sends to Libya. The reasons are as follows: (1) A 300-mile desert without water sources would leave attacking troops nowhere to escape British air attacks. (2) Lack of roads. (3) Armed Arabs riding back and forth are sufficient to endanger the Italian army's flanks. (4) British machine gun teams are densely deployed along the border, with barbed wire set up in front of their defenses for protection. (5) British and Egyptian soldiers have built trenches that are very thorough, and the British fleet off the Libyan coast can easily bombard Italian troops attacking from the north. Even if enemy troops attacking from the south can avoid British air attacks when crossing the desert, they will be bombarded by British machine guns and heavy artillery upon landing in Marsa Matruh. Beyond that, there are other natural barriers, and Alexandria is surrounded by gun emplacements, enough to contain the Italian army. Even if the Italian army attacks Egypt from the air, the British air force is strong enough to repel them. (Reuters dispatch, 30th)

Report from the New Commander of the Italian Army: Still Conducting Clearing Operations; The King of Afghanistan Inspects Progress on the Front Lines 44

(Rome) Today's gazette contains the first report from General Badoglio, the new commander-in-chief of Italian East Africa, after taking office. It states that the Italian army is still engaged in clearing operations in the Uolchefit area. An Italian column encountered armed Arabs on the west bank of the Qieba River. After a brief battle, the enemy retreated, abandoning ten bodies. Today, an Italian air squadron from the new Gura Hai airfield departed and continued to bomb Dagabur, destroying several transport vehicles. According to news from Asmara, Italian reconnaissance aircraft discovered a large Afghan army advancing north between Amba Aradam and Ashangi. It is also reported that the land occupied by the extreme left-wing Danakil column has not been completely cleared of Afghan soldiers. Italian aircraft in the area are often heavily bombarded by Afghan soldiers with machine guns. (Reuters dispatch, 30th)

Kabul The King of Afghanistan went to the northern front yesterday, but this news was only released today. The king quietly left the palace in a converted freight car, without any ceremony. The queen and two sons accompanied him to the suburbs. After the king embraced them, he went to Taixi. Soon, a large convoy of freight cars carrying the king's luggage and camping equipment departed from the capital. Six hundred guardsmen marched to Taixi three days ago to clear the road for the royal vehicle. After the king reviews the troops in Taixi, he will probably fly to the front lines. Crown Prince Hosain will remain in the capital to govern. (Reuters dispatch, 29th)

Progress on League of Nations Sanctions: Oil Embargo Against Italy to Be Implemented; Meeting to Vote on the 12th of This Month; Ban on Cotton and Copper Will Also Be Discussed 45

(Geneva) According to reliable sources, the chairman of the Committee of Eighteen, Portuguese representative Vasconcellos, after discussing with French Prime Minister Laval and British Minister without Portfolio Eden by telephone, has decided that the Committee of Eighteen should meet at 11:00 AM on December 12th. At that time, in addition to discussing the oil embargo, they will also discuss ways to ban cotton and copper from being shipped to Italy. The expert committees on the implementation of sanctions continued to meet today to review the implementation of various sanctions plans by various countries and will meet again tomorrow to discuss them. (Havas dispatch, 29th)

(London) Most diplomats here believe that the question of war and peace in Europe can be decided within a few days. Well-informed observers believe that Anglo-Italian relations are becoming more serious today, but most people still believe that Mussolini may not be able to resist the ban on oil, coal, iron, and steel from all over the world for a long time, or he may rein in his horse on the edge of the precipice and not take risks, causing Italy and all League of Nations member states to suffer from war. It was learned today that Mussolini's threats may not change Britain's attitude. The French Prime Minister is also determined to support Britain's position this time. (National Society Telegram, 29th)

(London) An oil embargo against Italy is inevitable. This move will greatly hinder Italy's war to develop colonies in East Africa. At the same time, according to a Reuters dispatch from Rome, the former Italian ambassador to France once notified French Prime Minister Laval that Italy would regard this move as a hostile act, but this has been denied by the Italian authorities. The attitude of Italian newspapers towards France is now very cautious and does not make remarks that would hurt French feelings. Currently, Italy has a total of 1,080,000 soldiers under arms. Rumors that troops stationed at the Brenner Pass have been transferred to the French border have been refuted by Rome as nonsense. According to a Reuters dispatch from Geneva, all parties related to the League of Nations regret that the Committee of Eighteen cannot meet before December 12. Now that it is heard that the issue of banning oil shipments to Italy is no longer a question of whether to implement it, but only waiting for a date to be selected, everyone is greatly relieved. People in Geneva now believe that if today's Italian cabinet meeting considers the issue of Italy withdrawing from the League of Nations, it is an expected matter and nothing to be surprised about. As a result of talks between the British Ambassador to Paris and French Prime Minister Laval, it is also felt that the French Prime Minister should declare to the Italian government that if Italy attacks British troops in the Mediterranean or elsewhere, France will come to Britain's aid. This assistance is based on the provisions of the League of Nations Covenant. This news has now been verified in London. Laval has notified Italy that France will follow Britain's position on the issue of banning oil shipments to Italy. Mr. Moffett, Vice President of Standard Oil of California, told guests in New York that if the US government asks oil companies to cut off Italy's oil supply, US oil companies are willing to stop selling oil to Italy. He also said that even if the list of prohibited items issued by President Roosevelt when declaring US neutrality does not include oil, the companies are willing to comply. (Reuters dispatch, 30th)

(London) Mr. Henderson, an expert on the Abyssinian question at the Foreign Office, is now in Paris discussing solutions to the Italo-Ethiopian dispute with Mr. Saint-Quentin, Director of East African Affairs at the French Foreign Office. He was originally scheduled to return home at the end of this week, but it is heard that the Foreign Office has instructed Henderson to remain in Paris. Our reporter also said that the British Foreign Office very much hopes that experts from Britain and France will draft a solution as soon as possible so that it can be submitted to the Italian government for discussion. (Havas dispatch, 30th)

Italian Cabinet Meeting: Difficulties of International Sanctions; Italian Representatives Visit Representatives of Eighteen Countries Separately; Expanding Sanctions Considered an Unfriendly Act 46

(Rome) The Italian cabinet held its first cabinet meeting today since the outbreak of war in early October. Officials said that this was a routine meeting and not a special convening of the government, but it is widely believed that the cabinet will study the difficulties caused by international sanctions. The content of the cabinet meeting was extremely confidential, but it was heard that Mussolini reported today on the results of the Chemical Society's research on increasing Italy's fuel supply. A communique was issued before the meeting, stating that the cabinet approved the government leader's proposal to expand the Supreme Defense Committee. The communique did not directly mention the war or the issue of sanctions. (Reuters dispatch, 30th)

(Geneva) The Secretary-General of the Italian delegation to the League of Nations visited the representatives of various countries attending the Committee of Eighteen yesterday and today, respectively, to personally present the League's proposed measures to enhance the effectiveness of sanctions against Italy, which Italy considers to be an unfriendly act. The representatives all promised to convey this opinion of the Italian government to their respective governments. (Havas dispatch, 30th)

(Rome) According to political sources, if an oil embargo against Italy is implemented, it will not be as serious as most people think, because Italy has already stored a large batch of oil, and consumption has been greatly reduced after the nationwide promotion of economical use of oil. Alternatives to oil are currently being researched and may be produced in large quantities by the beginning of next year. Therefore, even if various countries impose an embargo, there will be no panic. As for why Italy is doing its best to publicize and strongly oppose the oil embargo, it is actually because this move puts Italy in an embarrassing position psychologically. (Havas dispatch, 30th)

Port Said The Italian consulate here today advised overseas Chinese to deposit their savings in local banks and transfer them to the Italian consulate before December 15. Italians are currently busy applying for overseas accounts in the names of foreigners in order to avoid confiscation after the implementation of sanctions. Most overseas Italians are preparing to move to other places as soon as they receive a warning. (National Telegram, 29th)

(Rome) The recruitment of cavalry officers into the reserve today further proves that the European situation is becoming more serious after the implementation of economic sanctions against Italy. (National Telegram, 29th)

League of Nations Invites Philippines to Participate in Sanctions 47

(Geneva) The expert committee of the Committee of Eighteen on the implementation of sanctions continued to meet today. Considering that the Philippine Autonomous Constitution has been implemented, it was decided to negotiate with the new Philippine government to invite it to participate in sanctions against Italy along with the League of Nations member states. (Havas dispatch, 30th)

Naval Conference Invitation: League of Nations to Send Observers; British Representatives Selected; US Representatives Depart for England 48

(London) The naval conference is scheduled to be held on December 9, and everything is now prepared. An invitation has been sent to the Secretary-General of the League of Nations today, inviting them to participate in the conference as League of Nations observers, as was done at the 1930 London Conference. The British representatives are Foreign Secretary Hoare and First Lord of the Admiralty Monsell, assisted by Chief of the Naval Staff Chatfield, Permanent Secretary of the Treasury Fisher, Foreign Office Counselor Craigie, and former Fleet Commander James. (Reuters dispatch, 30th)

(New York) The United States delegation to the London Naval Conference, led by Chief Representative Norman Davis, Undersecretary of State Phillips, and Chief of Naval Operations Standley, departed from here on the mail ship "Ascania" for London. Norman Davis also declared before his departure that when the London Naval Conference is held, the representatives of the five countries, the United States, Britain, France, Italy, and Japan, will inevitably raise issues that will not be easy to resolve, but the United States delegation "will fully cooperate with all efforts aimed at establishing a new agreement." (Havas dispatch, 29th)

Roosevelt Addresses the Nation: Achievements in Economic Recovery; 3 Million People Have Found Work Since Taking Office; Increased Revenue and Reduced National Debt Without Imposing New Taxes; Continued Efforts to Improve the Lives of the American People 49

Atlanta President Roosevelt addressed the nation today, stating that the American economic recovery plan has been completed, and that the highest peak of spending has now been passed.

The President's speech was broadcast nationwide by radio and is generally regarded as Roosevelt's first move in the presidential election next year. The President's speech declared that 3 million people have found work since he took office. We no longer need to impose new taxes to increase revenue, and the budget deficit is expected to decrease. The government's credit is now better than any other country, but a few individuals and groups are trying to monopolize the nation's finances, disregard the poverty of the people, and damage the government's credit. In the spring of 1933, the national accounts proved that the entire property of the United States was not as great as the debts owed by the entire people of the United States. Today, the total debt has decreased compared to before, and the value of property has also increased sharply. We were on the verge of bankruptcy before, but now our credit is outstanding. However, recovery is by no means as simple as these figures can encompass. We look forward to the future and firmly believe that mankind's enjoyment will be better than in the past. The lives of Americans have clearly improved in the past two and a half years, but if we are concerned, we should redouble our efforts. Progress is better than recovery because it not only represents sound business, but also represents the sound progress of the lives of the American people.

The President then responded to those who criticized his fiscal policy, saying that you cannot borrow to pay off debt, but you can invest to expect a return. In the spring of 1933, the nation's bankers gathered in Washington to apply for assistance to avoid bankruptcy. At that time, I stated that in the next few years, the government would increase its debt burden to rescue banks, insurance companies, and railways, and to provide food and clothing for millions of people on the verge of starvation. At that time, everyone said that this was a very good plan. In order to seek their further judgment, I asked them what would be the maximum national debt that would not harm the nation's credit. They replied that the nation could bear a debt of 55,000,000,000 yuan to 70,000,000,000 yuan. I told them that there was no need for such a huge amount of money; a slight increase in debt would be enough, which is today's goal. But recalling that at that time, most bankers and big businessmen advocated a national debt that was far greater than what I had agreed to. Since the bankers of 1933 claimed that the government could bear a debt of 55,000,000,000 yuan to 70,000,000,000 yuan, then at a time when property prices are soaring, I really don't know what they would consider to be the debt that the government can bear. The previous government's debt increased by only 17,000,000,000 yuan to 21,000,000,000 yuan. This is a fact. When I took office, there was only 158,000,000 yuan in the treasury, which was not enough for a month's use. Since March 4, 1933, the national debt has increased from 21,000,000,000 yuan to 29,500,000,000 yuan, but about 1,500,000,000 yuan of which is working capital, and there are also 4,500,000,000 yuan of assets that can be converted into cash, both of which can be used to repay government bonds. The President then recounted the situation from 1924 to 1929, saying that at that time, speculation was rampant, banks collapsed, sacrificing the interests of depositors, farmers could not predict grain prices, slums were neglected, education was not paid attention to, interest rates were unusually high, child labor continued to exist, and wages were low. The situation was dangerous and unspeakable. After I took office, the government reopened banks, guaranteeing their deposits, correcting the extremely low wages of child labor, managing stock exchanges and public utilities, and designing to relieve floods and other natural disasters. The government is now formulating social security plans to seek the welfare of the masses. Regarding the future, the President said that although economic recovery has current achievements, the general public is still poor and can only afford to eat third-class food. If the general public can enjoy second-class or first-class food, arable land will naturally expand and agricultural product prices will also rise accordingly.

Regarding the relief plan, the President said that the gentlemen in the club are talking about their hardships because the government has allocated huge sums of money to carry out industrial revitalization. Unfortunately, they have little contact with the real America, so they cannot understand that those we treat are self-respecting Americans who believe that providing relief harms their independent nature. Although the President's speech may not immediately affect the market, the banking community has a good impression of it, because the government has hinted that it will reduce relief spending and find ways to make up for the budget deficit. However, the general public believes that this speech is a political declaration, not one directed at commerce. (National Telegram, 29th)

(Washington) The Federal Emergency Relief Administration was established with the approval of Congress on May 12, 1934, for a period of two years, stipulating that the central government and the states should cooperate to relieve the suffering of unemployment. Today, Mr. Hopkins, the director of the agency, stated that the agency has now been completely terminated, and that direct relief to the unemployed has now come to an end. Speakers consider this to be a victory for the government, with a total of 300 million yuan spent on relief since May 1933. There are still 4 million unemployed people who cannot be placed, and the government has stated that local authorities should be responsible for providing relief. Whether or not funds will be reallocated to cover this expense in the future, officials are currently unwilling to express an opinion. It is heard that some states have already received sufficient funds to continue providing relief for the time being. Today, President Roosevelt gave a speech to the citizens' congress in Atlanta, Georgia, stating that the government has employed 3,155,000 unemployed people in industrial revitalization projects, and that another 375,000 people have been instructed to report to the authorities to find work. Since the implementation of the method of replacing relief with work, there has been great progress in spirit, because engaging in relief destroys the spirit of independence. President Roosevelt is very optimistic about the weather next year, saying that the American economy continues to improve and has entered a prosperous path. Although there are no new speeches, the nation's income continues to increase, and the budget deficit can be gradually reduced. The credit of the US government is now higher than that of any country. In the past, our debts were greater than our assets, but today assets and debts can offset each other. (Reuters dispatch, 29th)

Discussions on Rural Life 50

— Edited by Yu Qingtang

The Rural Population and Rural Land of Jiangning Moling (Continued) 51

— Qiao Qiming, Jiang Jie

(V) Imbalance of Population and Land

In the past twenty-three years, the number of farm households has increased by one-half, while the cultivated land area has only increased by one-eighth. Therefore, the means of subsistence will inevitably increase slowly, while the number of consumers is increasing daily. In this process, the trend of farmers' lives is already more than half conceivable.

Now, let's analyze the figures to clarify the degree of its seriousness.

(I) Average Population per Household

The figures in the attached table are all statistics for this year, copied from the household registers kept by the heads of each town and village. Due to the Jiangning County Government's vigorous implementation of population census and registration, this material should be the most accurate. According to one town and four villages, the average population per household is 4.68 people, with very slight differences among the towns and villages.

Attached Table (I)

Average Rural Household Population in One Town and Four Villages of Jiangning, Jiangsu (1935 Survey)

Town/Village Name: Moling Town, Xiaoling Village, Renling Village, Xinling Village, Ailing Village, Total

Number of Villages Surveyed: 11, 14, 21, 36, 17, 89

Total Number of Households: 430, 581, 743, 1410, 826, 3990

Total Number of People: 2058, 2778, 3346, 6663, 3828, 18673

Average Population per Household: 4.79, 4.78, 4.50, 4.73, 4.63, 4.68

(II) Average Farm Size

Above, we used the total number of households in each town and village in 1934 to divide the total cultivated land area in 1934. We know that the average farm household in Moling Town has 12.4 mu of land, Xiaoling Village has 15.2 mu, Renling Village has 12.7 mu, Xinling Village has 8.0 mu, Ailing Village has 7.9 mu, and the overall average for one town and four villages is 10.4 mu. However, on our survey form, the original intention was to understand how many mu of land the majority of farm households can actually cultivate. Therefore, we asked, "What is the size of the most common farm in this village?" hoping that the answer with the highest frequency could represent the general reality and be more accurate than the average. The survey results showed that, except for Xiaoling Village, which has a slightly larger area of 19.1 mu, the others are all around 15 mu. The average for one town and four villages is only 15.9 mu. Details are in the table below:

Attached Table (II)

Average Common Farm Size per Household in One Town and Four Villages of Jiangning, Jiangsu (1935 Survey)

Town/Village Name: Moling Town, Xiaoling Village, Renling Village, Xinling Village, Ailing Village, Total

Number of Villages Surveyed: 11, 14, 21, 26, 17, 89

Total Common Farm Area: 174, 267, 324, 384, 264, 1413

Average Farm Area per Household: 15.8, 19.1, 15.4, 14.8, 15.5, 15.9

Attached Table (I) shows that each farm household has an average of 4.68 people, while the farm area in the above table is less than 16 mu per household. And in terms of the average, each household has only 10.4 mu. By comparing these figures, readers can know how serious the problem of the imbalance between population and land in the area is, and the impact of this imbalance on the lives of farmers is even more significant. This material will be published separately after analysis is complete, to provide further evidence.

(VI) Concluding Remarks

The population pressure in one town and four villages of Jiangning County is becoming increasingly serious, and the total land area is insufficient for cultivation. This is the biggest reason for the decline of the local rural economy and the hardship of farmers' lives! Moreover, the cultivable land is decreasing daily, while the population increase is in full swing. If this continues, the future worries will be even deeper!

In 1934, the author used the method of correspondence to investigate the trend of population and cultivated land increase and decrease in 22 provinces including Chahar over the past 60 years. The result showed that the population increase index was 131, while the land increase index was only 101 (see the Agricultural Report published by the Central Agricultural Experiment Institute). This is in line with the above survey of one town and four villages of Jiangning County, and the trends are similar. We believe that the people of the country should quickly wake up to this terrible reality! How to shift the focus of increasing population size to the path of improving population quality is the most urgent task. Other measures such as improving agriculture and increasing production are also important issues in terms of land. To complete this great mission, the initial work should be to promote a full recognition of this crisis among the people of the country, and those who are responsible for social education need to work even harder.
