Shortage of Copper Coins in Tianjin - Market Panic and Stagnant Turnover - 65

Tianjin Correspondence: Due to the unrest in Tianjin and rumors, the authorities are preoccupied with maintaining local security and have no time to take care of finance. Ten days ago, due to the order to replace cash with banknotes in Tianjin, a group of traitors took advantage of the rumors to make profits, resulting in soaring prices and a shortage of copper coins. The Municipal Government and the Public Security Bureau immediately tried their best to restrict high prices and stipulated that one national currency could be exchanged for 500 copper coins. At first, the shops in the Chinese Concession outwardly obeyed but inwardly disobeyed, all engaging in hoarding, causing the market price to remain between 460 and 470 coins per national currency. Later, after the Public Security Bureau arrested dozens of merchants who profited regardless of the overall situation and imposed fines and confiscated the hoarded copper coins, the market price became more stable. However, in various concessions, because the authority of the authorities did not reach, many still arbitrarily manipulated the market. The Belgian Tram Company also advertised that passengers must purchase tickets with copper coins, otherwise they would rather let people sit for free for one stop and ask them to get off at the next stop, and were unwilling to give change in copper coins. As the authorities are discussing with the banking industry to issue copper coin notes, and other pseudo-autonomy movements have emerged in the city, people are panicked. Certain foreigners took the opportunity to manipulate the market price and deliberately hoard copper coins, causing a shortage of copper coins and inconvenience in change, putting the poor in a difficult situation. With the riots breaking out, the copper coin exchange rate is even more chaotic. As of today, within the concessions, each yuan has been exchanged for 380 or 400 coins, and the highest price is no more than 430 coins. Outside the concessions, shops dare not violate the official legal price orders, so they all tend to absorb but not release. When purchasing goods with jiao notes, no matter how many copper coins are needed for change, they would rather sacrifice business and not let copper coins flow out. As a result, few copper coins circulate on the market, and most shops have to use stamps instead of cash, or issue paper slips with the words "a certain number of copper coins are stored." There are also those who use bamboo sticks to write the number of copper coins as a substitute. However, the paper slips and bamboo sticks issued by one store are not accepted by another store, and the poor find it very difficult to buy things. Unscrupulous merchants also use the issuance of paper slips and bamboo sticks as a pre-arranged transaction to do more business, imitating each other, almost becoming a fashion in the Chinese Concession. The inconvenient situation is beyond words. The Ninth District Autonomy Construction Office, in accordance with the merchants' wishes, convened a joint meeting of district directors on the 27th and decided to submit a request to the Municipal Government to urge the banking industry to issue copper coins as soon as possible to facilitate circulation, and to formulate a more effective method before the copper coin notes are officially issued to provide relief. Although the Tianjin Reserve Fund Custody Committee has been established, and the transport of cash from Tianjin to the south has been stopped, and the outflow has been effectively checked by the joint efforts of all parties, it has been confirmed that there is no causal relationship with the soaring copper coin price and the lack of spot goods.

Regarding the issuance of copper coin notes, after the leaders of the Tianjin Banking and Money Exchange Association discussed the results in Ping, a Hebei Provincial Copper Coin Note Issuance Reserve was specially formed, with branches in Tianjin and Baoding. The first batch of copper coins issued was agreed to be the old copper coin notes stored by the Hebei Provincial Bank that had not been issued, totaling 300,000 yuan, stamped with the seal of the reserve for substitute use. The capital totaled 200,000 yuan, jointly funded by the Tianjin Chamber of Commerce, the Tianjin Banking Association, the Tianjin Money Exchange Association, the Beijing Chamber of Commerce, the Beijing Banking Association, and the Beijing Money Exchange Association. Nineteen articles of the organization charter of the issuance reserve have been formulated. Zhou Zuomin has recently contacted the Hebei Provincial Bank, but there is no definite date when it can be implemented and circulated.

Jiangsu Provincial Government Strictly Prohibits Unscrupulous Merchants from Transporting Cash Silver Out of the Country. Designated Agencies for Exchanging Legal Tender are Ordered to Comply. Business is Active in Towns After the Implementation of the Legal Tender Policy. The Town Chamber of Commerce Sends Letters to All Banks to Release Pledge Loans as Much as Possible 66

Zhenjiang News: Since the central government implemented legal tender, unscrupulous merchants in various places have occasionally exchanged cash silver and secretly transported it. The Jiangsu Provincial Government has telegraphed all administrative commissioners' offices and county governments to strictly prevent this. Except for the cash silver transported by designated exchange agencies to the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications for exchange into legal tender, if private transportation of cash silver out of the country is discovered, it will be detained, the perpetrators will be arrested, and the matter will be investigated and dealt with seriously. In counties in this province where there are no branches of the Central Bank, Bank of China, or Bank of Communications, it is quite difficult to exchange legal tender. In addition to the exchange by county governments and collection agencies, the Provincial Government has also ordered the Jiangsu Bank and the Farmers Bank to exchange on their behalf. The designated counties are as follows: Wujiang, Qingpu, Gaocun, Liyang, Jiading, Yixing, Fengxian, Kunshan, Nanhui, Chuansha, Chongming, Baoshan, Jinshan, Lianshui, Dianhua, Suqian, Liuyang, Funing, Suining, Fengxian, Jiangning (all of the above counties are exchanged by the local Farmers Bank), Jingjiang, Xiaoxian (exchanged by both the Farmers Bank and the Jiangsu Bank), Pixian, Peixian (exchanged by the Xuzhou Farmers Bank), Lishui, Jiangpu, Jurong (exchanged by both the Nanjing Jiangsu Bank and the Farmers Bank), Yizheng, Yangzhong (exchanged by both the Zhenjiang Farmers Bank and the Jiangsu Bank), Siyang (exchanged by both the Qingjiang Jiangsu Bank and the Farmers Bank).

In addition, the Zhenjiang Chamber of Commerce believes that since the implementation of legal tender in this port, the market has shown obvious signs of activity. However, various shops have suffered from the impact of the recession for a long time and have been desolate. This adjustment is truly the grand purpose of enriching the country and benefiting merchants. Although commerce can be active, the key lies in financial turnover. At present, the banking industry, in view of the past state of social depression, mostly only stores and does not release, causing great blows to our commerce. Now that the legal tender policy has been implemented and commerce has become active, this chamber of commerce, in order to consider the difficulties of merchants, has decided to write to all banks requesting them to release pledge loans as much as possible in order to facilitate turnover and revitalize commerce. The standing committee will also convene the responsible persons of various banks to discuss methods to ensure the permanent activity of commerce. (27th)

Educational Broadcasting Special Issue

Efficiency and Methods of Elementary Education 67

— Wu Yan-yin, Section Chief of the Ministry of Education

Education is like manufacturing, and those who receive education are like manufactured goods. Manufacturers always hope to produce excellent products, and those in charge of education also hope to educate ideal citizens or talents. To produce excellent products, there must be good methods, that is, on the principle of economy, using the most economical methods to seek the greatest efficiency. The implementation of education is also the same; it must use the most economical methods to seek the greatest efficiency. Therefore, efficiency and methods are often related and linked. Simply wanting to obtain the greatest efficiency without considering methods often leads to groping in the dark, wasting manpower in worthless sacrifices, the so-called "twice the effort, half the result," "doing a lot of work but not pleasing anyone." Simply seeking changes in methods without considering the improvement of efficiency often results in emptiness and superficiality, which is also "doing a lot of work but not pleasing anyone." Therefore, methods and efficiency should be given equal importance and should be made into a direct proportional relationship.

Method is the necessary condition for organizing things, organizing things, and achieving understanding of certain things. If there is no method, the understanding of things will not be clear or correct. This is common sense that logic tells us. In education, method is equally important. Dewey said, "Method is the economical order of education." Once education has a goal, we must use the most economical method to achieve it.

Method is especially important in elementary education. Because the object of elementary education is children, and children are like a piece of uncultivated land. What kind of soil is suitable for planting what kind of plants in this piece of land? What kind of fertilizer should be applied? Everything must go through a series of investigations, observations, and experiments. Not only that, but because children's intelligence and physical strength have not yet fully developed, and their acquired experience and knowledge are not yet rich, so in teaching children, special attention should be paid to methods.

In the past few decades of elementary education in China, at first, methods were not emphasized. At that time, the general elementary schools in the cities were like most of the village elementary schools now, not paying attention to methods at all, only knowing how to instill, inject, and force memorization into children, reading books all day long; after children graduated, they only obtained a little knowledge from books, which had nothing to do with their life skills and had no effect. This kind of education, because it had no method, also had no real efficiency at all.

Of course, going on to higher education was still possible, and getting a job was still possible, but the citizens or talents cultivated at that time could not carry burdens on their shoulders or lift baskets in their hands; they were still just like the scholar-officials or quasi-scholar-officials who came from the imperial examinations, and they were not of much benefit to the country and society. After the first year of the Republic of China, we worked in the attached elementary school of the Jiangsu Provincial First Normal School in Suzhou. Because Mr. Yu Ziyi and others advocated it, we gradually began to pay attention to teaching methods. But the power was too isolated. At that time, many new methods being tried out in the attached elementary school of the First Normal School were often ridiculed as novelty tricks, and local elementary schools almost avoided contact with us. Later, the Nanjing Higher Normal School was established, and a group of students who had studied education in the United States returned to the country to work as teachers, greatly promoting new education. After the South Higher Normal School was changed to Southeast University, the wave of advocacy became even higher. The attached elementary school of the First Normal School and the attached elementary school of Southeast University were only slightly valued by people, and they were regarded as the source of new education. After Dewey came to China, the call for new education was even more "noisy," so elementary school teachers active in the Jiangsu area worked hard to study methods, so-called "project-based teaching method," "Dalton plan," "individualized teaching method," and what "cooperative teaching method," each trying to be innovative and using new methods to call for attention. At that time, books on the study of teaching methods were also published a lot, like bamboo shoots after a rain: for example, "Original Theory of Educational Methods," "Psychology of Learning," "Educational Psychology," "Curriculum Theory," "Children's Theory," really a lot. The child-centered and popularized elementary school textbooks, the surge in supplementary reading materials for elementary schools, and various scientific experiments on educational issues were all discovered during this period. It cannot be said that this was one of the most progressive periods in elementary education in our country. But this also seems to fit the old saying, "Everything has its advantages and disadvantages." Many elementary schools, because the methods have changed too much, the increase in efficiency is also very ordinary, and like playing tricks, there are indeed those who only change tricks and do not talk about reality. For example, every school implements the project-based teaching method, but "everyone can play magic tricks, but each has different skills." As a result, it is empty, superficial, and wastes a lot of math time in vain. After the success of the Kuomintang (?), some schools still study teaching methods; however, the efficiency has not been obvious, and a group of new members are one hundred percent distrustful, thinking that educational methods are also in the ranks of counter-revolutionaries being revolutionized; therefore, they are noisily only heard scolding "interest theory," scolding "education has no results," scolding "only knows how to imitate the United States," scolding "no central idea," scolding "only knows child-centered, forgetting national-centered (?)", even scolding "bird language and beast language," scolding "schools are not as good as private schools." Advocating restoration, advocating reading the Three Character Classic, advocating reading the classics, in short. It is really "liable to be blamed for every move." With such an atmosphere, methods naturally declined. When economic bankruptcy became acute, the promotion of joint examinations and random examinations, and the emphasis on reviewing homework by supervisors, elementary schools became factories that only sought fast production and good-looking forms. Being able to graduate early, pass the exam, and escape the criticism of the supervisors was considered to have achieved considerable efficiency in education. May I ask, what is the difference between this kind of efficiency and the educational efficiency of the late Qing Dynasty and the early Republic of China? We only need to compare the current efficiency of education with the goals of elementary education in our country to see the difference immediately. The goals of elementary education in our country are clearly analyzed in the curriculum standards promulgated by the Ministry of Education: First, to cultivate healthy physical bodies for children; second, to cultivate good character in children; third, to develop children's aesthetic interests; fourth, to increase children's life skills; fifth, to train children's work habits; sixth, to enlighten children's scientific thinking; seventh, to cultivate children's spirit of mutual assistance and unity; eighth, to cultivate children's concept of loving the country and loving the group. Now let us look at the results of children's education. Except for character and spirit, which are very difficult to see: First, according to the physical examinations in Shanghai and Nanjing, the results show that more than 80% of the children in school have diseases, indicating that the children's physical bodies are not healthy. Perhaps it is because they pay too much attention to reading, which has increased hunchbacks and nearsightedness. Second, they do paper work all day long, putting art, music, and crafts behind them; aesthetic interests have not been developed; life skills have not been increased; work habits have not been cultivated; and scientific thinking is even more impossible to talk about. As for the concept of loving the country and loving the group, it seems to have increased somewhat compared to before, but this cannot be entirely attributed to education; it can only be said that it is the result of the intensified oppression of external forces in recent years. We must know that the goals of elementary education cannot be considered reached by relying on excellent grades in daily exams and the large number of admissions to higher education; these efficiencies, at most, are just the acquisition of knowledge, and whether this knowledge is necessary for life is still a question.

Education should emphasize efficiency, and we must seek the greatest efficiency from the most economical methods. But how do we judge whether a method is economical or not, and whether the efficiency is large or not? Here, I will explain it again:

The first method of elementary education is to be based on psychology. Psychology tells us about the phenomena of mental life. The emergence of these phenomena is not accidental, but is related to innate heredity and acquired environment. Innate heredity, although not valued by most educators now in psychology, the difference in intelligence is still greatly related to heredity. For example, mental retardates and idiots are mostly caused by their parents or ancestors suffering from syphilis or mental illness. If educators do not understand this point and do not investigate this point clearly, and mistakenly treat ordinary children as mental retardates or idiots, then the teaching method will go astray and will not be economical. Environment is especially important in teaching methods: it is useless to talk to children in villages about cars and trams without showing them models or letting them experiment; after talking a lot, they may still be at a loss. It is useless to talk to urban children about farming and weeding without going to observe and work in the field, even if you describe it vividly, the children will still be at a loss. Making children at a loss is wasting children's mental energy, which is also very uneconomical.

Psychology also tells us that the order of psychological development is the association between stimulus and response. Therefore, we should give children appropriate stimuli based on their psychological development. For example, in teaching lower-grade children to recognize words, those who do not understand child psychology only know to teach children to read and write words; however, this method is not easy to generate efficiency, and forcing children to memorize words still results in forgetting. This is uneconomical. Psychology tells us: children's thinking is whole, and to recognize new things, we must use old experiences. For example, in teaching children to recognize words, the teacher does not have to use textbooks first, but can tell an interesting story or fact, and then the teacher can string together the important materials in the story into sentences and write them on the blackboard to make the children recognize the sentences. In this way, the sentences that the children recognize are related to what they have said, and it is much easier for them to learn. We all know that things related to ourselves are always easy to attract our attention, so we must tailor the teaching materials to children's lives. This is economical. Psychology can indicate many places where teaching methods can be used, but there is not enough time to list them all here. In short, the method based on child psychology is the most economical method, which cannot be argued.

Second, the method of elementary education must be based on biology. Biology can tell us the order of children's physical and mental development. The development of children's intelligence, emotions, reasoning ability, etc. all have a certain order. Fragile brains cannot withstand strong stimuli, and children with unrich understanding are naturally weak in reasoning ability. Therefore, children cannot understand classical Chinese during childhood, and cannot understand the great principles in the classics, history, philosophy, and collections. Children's physical bodies have not yet fully developed, and they cannot be asked to sit in the classroom all day long. Sexual function will definitely develop in the future. If they are not given a little sexual knowledge, they will be led astray in the future. Therefore, educators must also understand biology. Understanding children from the study of biology and making good use of methods is also the most economical method. Here is an additional explanation: that is, psychology is developed based on biology. In the past, biology was included in psychology. In recent years, they have been separated for study. The so-called experimental psychology is a major work in biology.

Third, the method of elementary education must be based on scientific experiments. The improvement of methods lies in experiments, and experiments must have scientific methods. Do not be superstitious about the ancients, and do not be slaves to the authority of anyone. All problems must be solved with scientific methods. For example, in Chinese language teaching methods, which is faster, reading aloud or reading silently? Which is more useful, reciting or understanding? Which is more convenient, checking dictionaries, radicals or numbers? We can all use scientific methods to experiment and find out the results, and then implement them. In this way, the efficiency of teaching can naturally be increased. Using scientific methods is also the most economical method.

As for examining the efficiency of elementary education, we also have two sciences to use as a basis: (1) to be based on pedagogy, (2) to be based on sociology. Pedagogy and sociology can both tell us the due goals of education. Psychology and biology are like the rudder and oars on a ship, which can make the ship turn left and right and move forward. Pedagogy and sociology are like the compass on a ship, which can indicate the direction of the ship. Pedagogy is also developed based on sociology. What kind of society, what kind of pedagogy is produced. What kind of society is China now? What should the education of our country be based on to establish goals? This is something that those who care about society and study society all know, and I will not say more about it.

Goals and efficiency cannot be confused. But the goal is a ruler, which can measure the amount of efficiency. So if we want to talk about the efficiency of education, we have to use goals as a measure.

Elementary education is a kind of preliminary education, and its object is immature children. Therefore, on the one hand, we must consider the efficiency of education, and on the other hand, we must pay attention to the methods of education. Otherwise, only seeking efficiency without method is really "fishing in trees"; on the contrary, only talking about method without talking about efficiency is also "a blind man riding a blind horse," so efficiency and method are inseparable. Finally, I repeat, "Education should use the most economical methods to obtain the greatest efficiency."

Songjiang: Xihutang Township Suffers Another Robbery 68

The home of Yu Zhuping of Jiuhu Township, Wu-jia, Erbao, Ba District, Punan, was suddenly attacked by six robbers speaking a local accent around 3:00 AM on the 28th while they were asleep. However, the Yu family was poor and only lost seven yuan in foreign currency and fourteen bolts of cloth. They left with the stolen goods after about half an hour.

Wuxi: Silver Coins Disappear from the Market 70

Since the Ministry of Finance issued an order nationwide to implement the non-convertible policy, unscrupulous merchants have seized the opportunity to seek personal gain at the expense of violating laws and regulations and harming the Republic of China. They have been buying up silver coins everywhere and reselling them to a certain country in order to make profits. Therefore, police stations in various counties have been uncovering cases of smuggling silver coins every day. In the Wuxi area, merchants have recently been privately collecting hard currency from various businesses, adding a premium of ten cents to thirty-seven cents per yuan. Fortunately, the public security authorities have strictly investigated and prohibited this, so there have been no thefts. Silver coins have now disappeared from the market and are mostly replaced by legal tender. However, silver coins have also disappeared, and the reason is that they have all been collected by unscrupulous merchants to hoard and speculate for profit. In view of this, the Public Security Bureau reissued instructions yesterday, strictly prohibiting unscrupulous buying and selling.

Seventh Robbers Arrested by the Ninth Precinct 71

Su Hongjun, the acting chief of the police patrol dormitory under the ninth precinct of the Public Security Bureau, led a police patrol near the Workers' Education Center at eleven o'clock the night before and arrested two thieves, Zhang Yugen and An Hanwen. They confessed that they had previously committed thefts at a tofu shop near Mahuang Bridge outside the West Gate and at the home of a certain family at Beizhakou, Huineng Bridge. An Hanwen also confessed that he had attempted to rob Da Songfen, Nannen County, with Wu Shunxing and Jin Zhixian five or six days ago, but failed. At the end of August, he also robbed Qiao Zhirong and Qiao Huirong of ninety-four yuan in paper money with Zhang Anan, Li Changfu, and Wen Lunren using a wooden pistol west of the Workers' Education Center in the West Gate. After obtaining the confession, Officer Su led the police to investigate and arrest the above criminals together. Since the case involved habitual thieves and was serious, they were immediately transferred to the General Bureau for interrogation.

Public Security Bureau Strictly Investigates Strange Advertisements 72

The local Wuxi newspaper published an advertisement on the 27th of this month for recruiting six secretaries, aged between 20 and 30, with a monthly salary of 60 yuan, located at No. 15 Sanhuang Street, signed by the Examination Committee. After this advertisement was published, many people applied and requested regulations because of the excellent treatment. After seeing the advertisement, the County Public Security Bureau, considering that its wording was vague and the so-called Examination Committee was unknown, sent a secretary, Fang Zhihao, to investigate secretly. It turned out that the head of the household there was Fan Yunzhang, who was ill and in debt. According to his niece, Chen Huifen, it was issued by Xie Qingyun, a friend of her brother Chen Tianjue. Xie lived in the Railway Hotel, etc. However, after waiting for a long time, he did not arrive. After inquiring at the Railway Hotel, they also said that he had disappeared. It was also heard that Xie was from Beiping, had previously studied at Soochow Middle School, and had just graduated from the Japanese Military Academy. He had been in Wuxi for a short time. The Public Security Bureau is now conducting a thorough investigation.

Yangzhou: Decision on Labor Service Measures 73

The Yangzhou County National Labor Service Conference decided on the following measures: (1) Participants, whether they are staff of government agencies, organizations, or schools, must abide by the provincial regulations and attached measures and serve at least three days per person. Merchants and residents must serve at least ten days per person. Everyone should provide their own tools. (2) The scope of service is divided into two items in the urban area: organizing municipal administration and organizing Slender West Lake. Municipal administration is served by citizens, and organizing Slender West Lake is served by staff of government agencies, organizations, and schools. In the second to seventh districts, the scope of service is three items: afforestation, road construction, and levee repair. In the eighth and ninth districts, the scope of service is four items: river dredging, pond opening, road construction, and afforestation. All are served by the people. Whether it is for road construction, levee repair, or river dredging, 50,000 cubic meters must be completed. The area of afforestation is determined temporarily. (3) Preparation for service: The urban area is presided over by the Construction Bureau, and the rural area is convened by the district offices. Organizations, groups, schools, and local people in the district convene meetings to discuss methods and implement them uniformly. The technical aspects of the project are negotiated with the Construction Bureau. (4) Mobilization date: The general mobilization of the county is scheduled to begin on December 1. All projects and implementation measures that should be prepared must be submitted to the county for approval by the Construction Bureau and district chiefs after November 25. (5) Payment standards: Party, military, police, government personnel, and school staff who cannot serve for factual reasons will pay one yuan per person. Merchants and residents who cannot serve for certain reasons are allowed to hire workers to replace them, or pay one corner of money per person per day, which will be used by the district to hire workers. (6) Other matters: The previously established measures and the projects to be done in each district are planned by the Construction Bureau and submitted to the provincial government for approval and filing, and then announced to the public.

Local News

Ministry of Finance: Supporting the Revival of Agriculture, Mining, Industry, and Commerce, Revitalizing the Economy, Instructing the Three Banks to Allow Agreements on Overdraft Limits with Various Banks 74

Regarding the proposals submitted by the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications on overdraft methods for fellow banks and incentive methods for fellow banks to collect cash currency, the Ministry of Finance has approved them for implementation. The instructions are as follows:

Letter to the Central Bank: A letter to the Central Bank states that the proposal submitted by Chen Guangfu and others, after joint discussion with the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications, on adjusting industrial finance and concentrating private cash, regarding four overdraft methods for fellow banks, one incentive method for fellow banks to collect cash currency, and three matters that the three banks themselves should discuss and decide, requesting instructions. After reviewing the four overdraft methods for fellow banks and one incentive method for fellow banks to collect cash currency jointly discussed by the three banks, it is found that they are feasible and should be approved for implementation. However, the use of this overdraft should be limited to the revival and development of agriculture, mining, industry, and commerce. As for (1) the total overdraft amount, it should be determined according to the needs of the market; (2) the share of the three banks should still be distributed according to the method of maintaining money market loans, with the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications sharing 4, 4, and 2; (3) joint custody of collateral and the establishment of overdraft accounts according to shares are appropriate. In addition to issuing instructions and separate orders, you are hereby requested to investigate and handle the matter in conjunction with the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications.

Order to the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications: An order to the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications states that a memorandum is submitted, jointly discussed by the three banks, on adjusting industrial finance and concentrating private cash, and the three banks themselves should discuss and decide on matters that should be jointly negotiated, requesting compliance. The memorandum has been read. After reviewing the four overdraft methods for fellow banks and one incentive method for fellow banks to collect cash currency jointly discussed by the bank with the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications, it is found that they are feasible and should be approved for implementation. However, the use of this overdraft should be limited to the revival and development of agriculture, mining, industry, and commerce. As for (1) the total overdraft amount, it should be determined according to the needs of the market; (2) the share of the three banks should still be distributed according to the method of maintaining money market loans, with the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications sharing 4, 4, and 2; (3) joint custody of collateral and the establishment of overdraft accounts according to shares are appropriate. In addition to issuing instructions and separate orders, this order is issued to order you to comply and handle the matter in conjunction with the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications.

Order to Chen, Zhou, etc.: An order to Chen Guangfu, Chairman of the Shanghai Banking Association, and Zhou Zuomin, Chairman of the Beiping Banking Association, states that the memorandum on adjusting industrial finance and concentrating private cash previously submitted in person, regarding promoting legal tender, collecting cash, and supporting the development of agriculture, mining, industry, and commerce, is quite important and has been handed over to the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications for joint review. A reply is now recorded stating that the three banks have been convened to jointly discuss the measures and are now submitting them separately as follows: (1) Fellow banks requesting overdrafts from the three banks should submit in writing the types of collateral, the value of the overdraft amount, and the overdraft period for review by the three banks. (1) The six items of overdraft collateral originally proposed: (A) public bonds, treasury bills, and certificates approved for issuance by the central government; (B) commercial paper and import and export bills of exchange; (C) real estate, industrial plants, factory machinery, factory buildings, and bases; (D) goods warehouse receipts; (E) bonds, treasury certificates, and public bonds issued by the joint preparatory committee of the Shanghai Banking Association; (F) bonds of companies with reliable guarantees and listed company stocks. Of the above six items, except for item (C), the other five items (A, B, D, E, F) can be accepted. Regarding item (C) collateral, it should be stipulated that it has been reviewed and certified by the three banks as having been done before this measure, and a formal valuation certificate must be submitted. (1) All procedures for overdraft collateral should be handled in accordance with precedents. (1) During the overdraft period, if the market's chips are loose, the three banks plan to consider the situation and negotiate with the overdraft parties to reduce the amount or return it. (1) In order to encourage fellow banks to collect cash currency, it is proposed that after fellow banks deliver 60,000 yuan in cash currency, they will be allowed an overdraft amount of 40,000 yuan. The overdraft parties should submit collateral and sign an overdraft contract. After reviewing, it is found that it is feasible and should be approved for implementation. The total overdraft amount should be determined by the three banks based on the needs of the market and allocated according to shares. However, the use of this overdraft should be limited to the revival and development of agriculture, mining, industry, and commerce. In addition to issuing orders to the three banks to handle the matter jointly, you are hereby notified and instructed to pass this on to all fellow banks.

Petition for Relief of Domestic Industry 78

Presented by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce: The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday presented a petition to the Ministry of Finance stating: This petition concerns a matter of factual reporting. On the 25th of this month, we received a letter from the Shanghai Steamship Industry Association stating that recently, industry and commerce have been declining, all trades are in decay, imports are increasing daily, production is decreasing daily, resulting in the city's financial situation being on the verge of collapse. Fortunately, our government has seen this and has reformed the currency system, resolutely implementing orders. Since the announcement, the economy has shown activity, and foreign exchange has gradually stabilized. This is indeed a good sign of turning danger into safety. The government, in order to supply the needs of industry and commerce, will reform and improve the banking system, find ways to increase its liquidity, so that its capital is abundant, and will also establish real estate mortgage banks and amend real estate mortgage laws to revitalize real estate. This is an especially good policy for saving the times and a crucial plan for economic recovery. All our merchants and people praise it in unison. We have found that economic recovery begins with revitalizing industry. To revitalize industry, it is necessary to reduce interest rates first. Now the government's economic concentration, for the purpose of establishing special banks and setting minimum interest rates specifically to relieve industry, is more than capable. However, although the plan has been predetermined, it has not yet been put into practice. It is urgent that various groups convene to discuss and petition the government to implement it as soon as possible, in order to help industry and avoid missing the opportunity. For this reason, we have prepared this letter and respectfully request that you consider it carefully and promptly convene various industry associations to hold practical discussions and jointly devise a plan. This matter was submitted to the 70th regular meeting of the affiliated associations on the 28th of this month for discussion. Everyone agreed that since the implementation of the currency management policy, reserves have been concentrated, and the economy has gradually stabilized. However, upon reviewing various domestic industries, there is still a lack of funds, and they have not been able to flourish. It is imperative to find ways to provide relief. It was resolved to forward this matter to your ministry for review and instructions. As for the request to convene various industry associations for discussion, it will be postponed temporarily. Meanwhile, letters will be sent to various industries to solicit opinions, which will be compiled and reported to your ministry for decision. These matters have been recorded and are now reported to you. We respectfully request your review and instructions, as this would be in the public interest.

Presentations from Various Associations: Seventy-odd trade associations, including the Yarn Industry Association, dispatched representatives Gu Xinyi, Lao Jingxiu, Luo Qinghua, Wen Lanting, Zhu Wenqi, Zheng Chengqing, Ke Ganchen, Jin Runxiang, Ma Jiliang, Zhou Bangjun, and ten others at 11:00 AM yesterday morning. They carried a petition to the Central Bank to petition Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi for relief of industry. Deputy Minister Xu Kan received them. First, the representatives described the state of decline of Shanghai's industry and commerce and requested: (1) Order the Central Bank to handle rediscounting; (2) Order the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications to re-mortgage real estate, such as factory land and factory property. Deputy Minister Xu agreed to handle rediscounting and stated that arrangements had been made with various banks for real estate mortgages, with the three banks providing overdraft facilities to various banks. At 1:00 PM, Minister Kong Xiangxi received them. He stated that the Central Bank would handle rediscounting immediately and that the market situation would stabilize after the end of the Gregorian calendar year, with no problems anticipated. They left at around 2:00 PM, and the results were very satisfactory.

Business Leaders Meet with Kong: Shanghai industrialists Yu Qiaqing, Liu Hongsheng, Rong Zongjing, Guo Shun, Nie Lusheng, and five others went to the Central Bank at 11:00 AM yesterday morning to meet with Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi to petition him. They were received. First, Yu Qiaqing described the state of decline of industry and commerce and requested: (1) Please ask the government to quickly establish special banks, or first have the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications allocate large sums of money to relieve industry so that various business owners can fully utilize all their capital; (2) Please ask the Central Bank to lower market interest rates and find ways to recover high-interest bonds to encourage the general public to invest in industry. They left at 12:00 PM. A reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency met with Yu, Liu, Rong, and others at the Central Bank. They said that the results of the meeting were very satisfactory.

Municipal Public Security Bureau: Re-census Completed; Card Compilation Work to be Finished Within the Year 79

The Municipal Public Security Bureau's re-census, which began on the 16th, ended yesterday. The bureau plans to compile household and individual cards from the collected materials within this month. Individuals with criminal records will also have special cards made for investigation purposes. The compilation will be completed within the year. The details are reported below:

Re-census Completed Yesterday

In order to understand the living conditions and activities of the people of Shanghai and to distinguish between good and bad, the Municipal Public Security Bureau launched a city-wide re-census on the 16th of this month. Teams, squads, and groups were organized, mobilizing over 1,100 police officers. Within the jurisdictions of each branch bureau and station, police officers distributed household survey forms to ordinary households, boat dwellers, and temples. Public places and foreigners were sent letters requesting them to fill out designated survey forms. As of yesterday, the household survey forms have been collected in order, and public places and foreigners have also submitted them. Therefore, the re-census survey work can be considered complete.

Card Compilation Work to be Completed Within the Year

After the survey work is completed, the bureau plans to spend the time from the beginning to the end of this month compiling the cards, aiming to complete the work within the year. First, the submitted survey forms will be sorted, and then household cards and individual cards will be compiled. The front of the household card will include the householder's name, whether they own or rent, the branch bureau, police station, sub-station, or police post, street, road, lane, block, house number, household members' titles, names, aliases, genders, ages, native places, occupations, workplaces, party affiliation, religion, education levels, date of arrival in Shanghai, disabilities and special physical characteristics, and whether they smoke opium or substitutes. The back will include the date and address of relocation: year, month, day, residing at branch bureau, police station, sub-station, or police post, road, lane, block, or street, alley, house number. Individual cards are divided into two types: ordinary individual cards (males marked with blue lines, females marked with red lines), with the front including the name, householder's name, and relationship.

Our overseas Chinese compatriots in various ports of Southeast Asia, whether British, Dutch, or French, are numerous. Overseas Chinese compatriots are deeply affected abroad, and their patriotism must be even stronger. The sales of domestic goods in Southeast Asia should be developed, but they have gradually decreased recently, and the entire market will be completely taken over by other countries. In October of this year, the Singapore Chinese Chamber of Commerce held a large-scale domestic goods exhibition and promotion conference. However, due to insufficient preparation time, in addition to the hundreds of companies that provided exhibits, not many others sent representatives to promote goods. Our association and others deeply regret this. All the details can be reported in detail by Consul-General Song. Our association and others can tell Consul-General Song about the preparations. In short, in Batavia, all matters will be handled by the three major organizations in Batavia; in Shanghai, all matters will be handled by our association to the best of our ability. Regarding funding, the Batavia side has already raised 2,000 to 3,000 Dutch guilders, which will cover the construction of the venue and electricity costs. However, in Shanghai, the expenses for preparations, the accommodation for representatives in Batavia, and the venue layout will require government funding. We wonder if Consul-General Song had any practical solutions after discussing this with the Minister of Industry in Beijing. As for the points that Consul-General Song should pay attention to during the preparation, (1) the types and quantities of goods that can be sold in Batavia must be accurately determined, (2) the import tax rates and price standards in the Dutch East Indies must also be determined to give manufacturers a sufficient grasp and enable sales, (3) the issue of import taxes must be resolved in advance, (4) the issue of discounted shipping (how many people are limited), (5) other measures can be referred to the Singapore Domestic Goods Exhibition.

Mr. Song's Reply: Gentlemen, during this return to China, before my departure, the Dutch East Indies Commercial Federation and other three organizations, in order to actively expand the sales of domestic goods overseas, requested that I ask the central government for subsidies to build a China Pavilion in Batavia to promote domestic goods. It is scheduled to open at the end of August next year during the Dutch East Indies National Day. Because the Annam government has established an Annam Pavilion there for many years to exhibit products, and the results are excellent, the overseas Chinese hope that domestic manufacturers can also go to the Batavia night market to promote domestic goods. After my return to China, I will report everything to Minister Chen. The Minister's opinion is that he strongly supports the expansion of publicity for domestic goods, but due to the central government's finances, he intends to ask the factories to raise their own funds. The consulate can find ways to reduce freight and half-price tickets. At the same time, the overseas Chinese will provide 3,000 guilders as part of the expenses for manufacturers to go abroad. The rest will be borne by the participating manufacturers. Because domestic goods have almost no status in the Dutch East Indies, if this can become a reality, it will not only allow overseas Chinese to recognize domestic goods but also develop foreign trade. I am very honored to be hosted by the Commercial Federation and the Chamber of Commerce. Then Wang Zhisheng reported on his participation in the Singapore National Exhibition. The gathering ended happily at 9:00 PM.

Scheduled Departure: Consul-General Song is scheduled to take the overnight express train to Beijing at 11:00 PM today to seek instructions from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. He will stay for about two or three days and come to Shanghai on the 4th. On the 5th, he will take the Java Line's Zhisha Danni to leave the country. The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce of this city are preparing to participate in the Batavia China Pavilion Domestic Goods Exhibition, so it has been decided to convene the city's factory groups to discuss participation methods.

Eurasia Company's Xi'an-Lanzhou Section Airplane Accident Reported Yesterday; Cause Still Under Investigation; Decision to Switch to Giant Aircraft 81

Yesterday's report of the Eurasia No. 5 aircraft that crashed about ninety kilometers southeast of Pingliang stated that two passengers were injured, and the pilot and mechanic were unfortunately killed. It is now reported that the pilot's name was Xia Lomm, 26 years old, born in Thuringia, Germany. He studied mechanics, telecommunications, and aircraft piloting at the German Civil Aviation School for four years. In 1932, he was introduced by Lufthansa of Germany to Eurasia Airlines as a flight mechanic and telegraph operator, totaling 370,000 kilometers of flight. In the summer of this year, he was promoted to aircraft pilot, flying between Peiping, Zhengzhou, and Lanzhou Baotou, totaling 47,000 kilometers of flight. The mechanic who died at the same time was named Meier, 32 years old, born in Frankfurt, Germany. In 1933, he was introduced by Lufthansa to China and served as a flight mechanic and telegraph operator at Eurasia Airlines, totaling 342,000 kilometers of flight. The cause of the plane crash is still under investigation. It is reported that Eurasia Airlines, in view of the dangerous terrain and unpredictable weather between Xi'an and Lanzhou, will disregard profits and losses and has decided to immediately switch to using three-engine giant aircraft to fly that section. It also telegraphed Germany today to continue renting a giant aircraft, ordering it to fly to China immediately to supplement the fleet.

Zhending Cotton Mill Manager, Zhao Dexiong Commits Suicide; Tragically Failed, Struggled to No Avail; Reportedly Related to Courtesan Miss Zhou Manli 82

Zhao Dexiong, the manager of Zhending Cotton Mill, had a wide circle of friends and was a business tycoon. During the outbreak of the European War in 1917, the source of dyes was scarce, and supply could not meet demand. Zhao Dexiong happened to be operating a dye shop in the interior. With his keen vision, he had accumulated a large amount of indigo blue, which he took the opportunity to sell, immediately reaping huge profits. After becoming rich, Dexiong moved his entire family to Shanghai, hired workers to build a mansion, and connected with local celebrities. Furthermore, in connection with the relationship of repaying military expenses, he formed a sworn brotherhood with General Li Xueyuan. General Li was in a position of power at that time, and everything went smoothly. Dexiong, with his help, then used the theory of saving the country through industry to call on the public to establish Zhending Cotton Mill. Sure enough, with effective management, the business developed day by day. Thus, it increased from one factory to two, then to three, four, and five. However, after the end of the European War, foreigners returned to Shanghai and invested in competition, which became increasingly fierce. Domestic industries suffered blows, and Chinese cotton mills were especially affected. Although Zhao Dexiong struggled, because General Li had already retired and the financial community was seeking self-preservation, he was stretched thin. Dexiong had a relative, Ke Zhi, who had followed him for many years and was quite loyal. Recently, Ke Zhi took the money north to purchase food, hoping for a last-ditch effort to reverse the situation. Suddenly, the sky darkened, and Ke Zhi died in the disaster. Thus, all plans were exhausted, and Zhao Dexiong tragically failed. Zhao Dexiong had been overly stimulated over the years, leading to madness and suicide. It is also rumored that Zhao Dexiong's suicide was due to various reasons, and the courtesan Miss Zhou Huanli, who was his English secretary, was also related. In short, the plot is tortuous and full of dramatic elements, making it good material for a script.

The above is the general plot of the Yihua Company's talkie giant film "Hero of the Times," which will soon be screened at the Jincheng Grand Theater. The film is directed by Mr. Ying Yunwei and stars Hu Ping, Shang Guanwu, Ma Loufen, Ye Juanjuan, Wan Laitian, etc. The results are excellent, especially as the most glorious harvest of domestic films in 1935. As the screening period approaches, we hope people from all walks of life will pay attention.

Ministry of Industry: Measures to Revitalize Industry and Commerce; Request to the Municipal Government for Implementation 86

The Ministry of Industry stated that in view of the declining state of domestic industry and commerce, in order to revitalize them, it has formulated methods that combine both symptomatic and fundamental treatments, implementing controlled trade, promoting domestic goods, and advocating thrift, and has communicated these to the municipal government for earnest implementation in order to revive the national economy. The measures are described below:

Controlled Trade: The Ministry stated that since the domestic economic organization is not sound and industry and commerce are declining, the way to provide relief is to focus on trade regulation to reduce the outflow of cash. It has formulated methods for controlled trade, divided into three steps: (1) Revising tariff rules to increase import tariffs, prevent the dumping of cheap foreign goods, and prevent domestic industry and commerce from suffering damage. (2) Export controls and sound industrial and commercial organization. The state manages the quantity, price, and quality of goods produced according to market supply and demand to meet the conditions of foreign markets. Industries should seek cooperation, mutual financial assistance, and avoid unnecessary competition. There should also be a sound organization to remedy weaknesses in business. Export trade should gradually not rely on foreign merchants. (3) Import restrictions. Our country's current crisis is recognized by all countries. People's purchasing power is decreasing, and imports must also gradually decrease. If, unfortunately, the Chinese economy suffers a final collapse, the business of all countries in China must also come to an end. If import restrictions can be implemented to restore the domestic economy, the business of various countries in China will also benefit, with common prosperity and mutual reliance.

Promoting Domestic Goods: The Ministry stated that the promotion of domestic goods has been implemented for a long time but has not had a deep and significant effect. The important reasons are: (1) it is affected by exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies and domestic disasters, (2) it is due to the lack of patriotism among the people. In the future, we should strive for (1) the complete abolition of exorbitant and miscellaneous taxes to remove the shackles on production. Although local governments cannot thoroughly cut exorbitant and miscellaneous taxes due to financial difficulties, the people's productive enterprises cannot develop, and industry and commerce and finance will fall into ruin. We should supervise local officials to focus on reducing the burden on merchants and the people. (2) The stimulation of the people's patriotism is of great importance. We should have the spirit of strongly supporting national plans, sacrificing personal enjoyment, and purchasing domestic goods to promote the development of domestic goods.

Thrift Movement: The Ministry stated that when the country and the people's economy are impoverished, consumption should be reduced to save them from danger. Currently, domestic industry and commerce are not developed, and the level of national life is increasing day by day. The general inability to produce affects the unemployed, which are countless. However, urban people are accustomed to using foreign goods, and the result of expanded consumption is that most of the money flows out. Domestic goods are sluggish due to poor sales and cannot recover. We should urgently promote the national thrift movement, implement self-sufficiency, reduce the import surplus of foreign goods, and save the collapse of the national economy.

U.S. Consul General in Shanghai, Mr. Cunningham, Retired Yesterday, to be Temporarily Replaced by Mr. Davis 88

The "Great American Evening Post" reports that Mr. Cunningham, the U.S. Consul General in Shanghai, who has served for sixteen years, officially retired today (30th) and is preparing to return to his country on December 21st. Mr. Cunningham has been in the U.S. consular service for thirty-eight years, having served in Aden, Berchem, Bombay, Singapore, Hankou, and other places. From December 1st, Mr. Davis, the former U.S. Consul General in Stockholm, Sweden, will temporarily take charge of the Shanghai U.S. Consulate. Mr. Davis has been in the Shanghai office for almost a year. Mr. Cunningham has been the head of the consular corps in Shanghai for ten years. From tomorrow, this position will belong to Mr. Aall, the Norwegian Consul General in Shanghai. From tomorrow, Mr. Cunningham will be taking care of personal matters, visiting friends, and packing his luggage. After arriving in the U.S., he plans to return to his hometown of Menominee, Michigan, with no other plans. Mr. Cunningham told a friend today, "I am now retired, so I have no plans." He also said that besides knowing that the position of U.S. Consul General will be temporarily taken over by Mr. Davis, he had not heard who the successor would be. According to regulations, Mr. Cunningham's term should expire on December 31st. The report that Mr. Jacobs will succeed Mr. Cunningham was found to be inaccurate after investigation today. Mr. Jacobs previously served in China. On July 2, 1934, he was transferred to be a Foreign Affairs Inspector, with the title of Consul General. He has traveled to the Near East, India, the Straits Settlements, and other places. It is said that he is currently en route to Australia and will come to China to inspect consular affairs, but will not arrive before next spring. As far as the officialdom knows, Mr. Jacobs has not been appointed to any specific position in Shanghai, but is only coming here for inspection. Mr. Davis has also served as a Foreign Affairs Inspector and has extensive experience in consular affairs. He has a wide circle of friends in Shanghai, and his friends have already congratulated him on taking up the new position today.

Forced Registration of Smokers Ends This Month; Second Round of Raids Today 91

The Public Security Bureau ordered all branches to intensify crackdowns, according to Da Gong She. Since the Shanghai Public Security Bureau began the forced registration of smokers last month, it has worked hard on publicity, persuasion, and crackdowns, with significant results. Now that the deadline for forced registration is approaching at the end of this month, the bureau, in order to avoid any loopholes, has decided to conduct a second round of raids starting today and is actively preparing to establish a smoking cessation hospital, which is to be established before the 15th of this month. In addition, the city's youth propaganda team is also scheduled to hold an expanded anti-smoking propaganda campaign on the 4th. Details of the situation are recorded below:

Forced Registration Ends This Month

The registration of smokers in this city is carried out in accordance with the regulations issued by the Chairman's Office of the Military Affairs Commission for the registration of smoking households within a specified period. It started on July 1st of this year, with smokers registering voluntarily. Forced registration started on October 1st. Over the past five months, nearly 30,000 smokers have voluntarily registered or have been found and ordered to register by the Public Security Bureau, of which more than 4,000 have applied for treatment. As of yesterday, in addition to the 2,250 people who have already been sent for treatment and the 1,669 people who have quit smoking, there are still more than 2,000 people waiting to be sent for treatment. The bureau has now decided to stop registration at the end of this year. From January 1st next year, smokers who are found to have not registered will be punished according to regulations and will be detained and forced to quit.

Second Round of Raids Starts Today

In addition to expanding the publicity of the dangers of smoking, investigating smokers, and persuading them to register, the bureau is also very active in cracking down on smoking. In addition to ordering all branch offices to pay attention to the arrest, and assigning personnel to conduct regular inspections at all land and water transportation docks, a special crackdown team has been established. The first crackdown started on the 5th of last month and ended on the 20th, resulting in the arrest of more than 800 smoking offenders, with excellent results. The second crackdown has been scheduled to start today. Yesterday, orders were specifically issued to police officers in various branches to strictly investigate and assist in the crackdown to avoid loopholes. It is reported that the crackdown will last for one month. After the forced registration ends, crackdowns will continue at any time, and privately operated smoking dens will be strictly investigated to thoroughly eliminate them.

Smoking Cessation Hospital Established Mid-Month

The bureau previously believed that the North and South Shanghai Smoking Cessation Hospitals were not sufficient to accommodate smokers, so it specially requested approval from the municipal government and the health bureau to jointly establish a large-scale smoking cessation hospital. Wu, the section chief of the Health Bureau, and Dai, the section chief of the Public Security Bureau, surveyed the Gaojing New Village in Jiangwan as the hospital site and drafted a plan and budget, which were submitted to the municipal government for approval. Because the required funds were more than 70,000 yuan, which was difficult to raise, representatives from the Public Security Bureau, Health Bureau, and Finance Bureau were specially convened a few days ago to discuss solutions. It was decided to submit another report for the municipal government to review and handle. Dai, the section chief of the Public Security Bureau, went to the municipal government yesterday to discuss the matter. According to reports, it is still under review and is expected to be established before the 15th of this month to facilitate the sending of smokers for treatment.

Various Groups Assist with Propaganda

The city's youth propaganda team believes that the government's current registration of smokers and the practical ban on smoking are of great significance. In order to show its assistance, the team has agreed with the City Anti-Smoking Association to conduct propaganda. Members have been dispatched to give lectures and persuade people to quit smoking, and they have been very busy. The team has also scheduled a propaganda conference for 7:00 PM on the 4th to expand the propaganda. In addition, the City Public Education Center is also planning to organize a lecture team and a teaching team, using the "little teacher system" to assist the government in its anti-smoking propaganda. The various methods are currently being drafted and will be established and begin work within days.

Bank Association Discussed Acceptance Bills Again Yesterday 95

The Shanghai Banking Association has established a sub-committee to study the promotion of commercial acceptance bills and has formulated several measures. It is reported that the association also raised this matter for discussion at the routine bank symposium held at 5:00 PM yesterday. In order to gather ideas from all parties, Zhu Boquan, the manager of the Banking Joint Preparation Committee, was specially invited to attend and contribute his opinions in order to be thorough. It is reported that in principle, this matter has absolutely been agreed upon by all parties. However, regarding the procedures, whether it will be handled by the Shanghai Industry and Commerce Loan Review Committee, or by each bank separately, or whether a specific bank will be designated to handle it on behalf of others has not yet been decided. Generally speaking, the Banking Association will consolidate the opinions of all parties, submit them to the Executive Committee for discussion, and then reply to the Industry and Commerce Loan Review Committee for review and implementation.

Belgian Modern Art Exhibition Opened Yesterday; Mayor Wu Tiecheng Was Specially Invited to Officiate the Opening Ceremony; Ministers and Consuls from Various Countries Attended 96

The Shanghai exhibition of the Belgian Modern Art Exhibition opened at 2:30 PM yesterday at the Hamilton Building at the intersection of Fuzhou Road and Jiangxi Road. Chinese and foreign visitors were very enthusiastic and praised the exhibition in unison. Details are recorded as follows:

Arrangement of the exhibition. The exhibition venue is on the ground floor of the building. Entering through the main entrance on Fuzhou Road, it is divided into five rooms. All exhibits are hung on the walls, totaling 131 pieces, divided into types such as oil paintings, watercolors, pastels, and charcoal paintings, with oil paintings accounting for the majority. There are landscapes, human figures, and still lifes, a dazzling array of beautiful things. The arrangement is orderly, with Cao Shanming in charge of taking care of the venue. The Belgian Minister to China, Monsieur de Kerchove d'Exaerde, led the Consul General in Shanghai, M. Tan Erfu, Consul M. D'ellez, Secretary Cheng Yinglin and others to personally receive guests.

Attendees. The Belgian Legation in China specially invited Mayor Wu Tiecheng of this city to officiate the opening ceremony, but no ceremony was held. Mayor Wu arrived at 3:00 PM and then officiated the opening. From 2:00 PM in the afternoon, people continued to visit, and by 6:00 PM in the evening, there were no less than 500 people. Among the Chinese and foreign officials who attended, in addition to Mayor Wu, were Yu Ming, Director of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Shanghai Office, Xu Peihuang, Director of the Municipal Public Works Bureau, Zhang Tingrong, Secretary of the Municipal Government, Reitan, the Swiss Chargé d'Affaires to China, Shao Xin, the French Commercial Counselor to China, and other officials from various agencies, as well as many ambassadors, ministers, and consuls from various countries in Shanghai.

Competition for Works. Among the works, the most valuable is the oil painting "Girl" No. 9, which was sold for 1,215 yuan and has been purchased by Chairman Lin of the National Government. The lowest is the charcoal drawing "Child's Posture" No. 44, which was sold for 15 yuan. Mayor Wu specially purchased the oil painting "Landscape" No. 127 yesterday. In addition, the following works were purchased during the previous exhibition in Nanjing: Mayor Ma Chaojun of Nanjing purchased the landscape painting No. 8, Chairman Lin purchased two paintings of landscapes and portraits of the King No. 35, the Belgian Minister purchased the Australian Woman No. 24, the Japanese Consul General Suma purchased the flower painting No. 47 and the View from Above No. 94, the Central University purchased two paintings of flowers and landscapes No. 49, the President of the Examination Yuan Dai Chuanxian purchased the still life No. 28, the still life No. 29, and the Mediterranean Coast No. 78, for a total of three paintings, the President of the Legislative Yuan Sun Ke purchased the Spanish Woman No. 121, the Winter of Poland No. 126, and the three paintings before Flowers No. 65. Wang Tingzhang purchased Napoleon I's tea set No. 3, etc. In addition, the Reflection No. 20 was also purchased yesterday by Mr. Heth of the Sino-Belgian Gengkuan Society.

Welcome to Visit. The exhibition will be open for ten days from yesterday to the 9th, from 10:00 AM to 6:00 PM every day, welcoming people from all walks of life to visit and critique. However, in order to limit idlers, admission tickets will be sold for two jiao per person from today.

Tongcheng Vessel Aground in Anhui; Vessel Dispatched Today for Rescue 97

Aground Due to Fog. The Tongcheng, a vessel of the local Tongcheng Steamship Company, which is used to transport cargo and coal, was sailing downstream from Tongzibao in the upper reaches of the river. When it reached about twelve nautical miles downstream of Anqing, it encountered heavy fog and the pilot misread the channel, causing it to run aground on a shoal downstream of Anqing. Because it was carrying a large amount of cargo, it became deeply embedded. This happened on Thursday afternoon.

Unable to Escape. After running aground, the Tongcheng shipowner wanted to escape on his own, but he had lost the ability to move. He telegraphed Shanghai for help. The company notified the insurance association, and immediately tried to send a ship to rescue it. However, the water was too shallow and the load was too heavy, so the rescue was unsuccessful.

Dispatching a Vessel to Unload Cargo. Yesterday, because the towing was unsuccessful, the Tongcheng Company informed the China Shipping Insurance Federation and discussed other methods. In the afternoon, Tang Danhua, the director of the Federation, said that Tang had agreed with Kang Zhengji in this city yesterday afternoon to allow the dispatch of a barge from Shanghai to Anqing today to open the hatch and unload the coal carried by the Tongcheng vessel to reduce the weight of the ship and then try to tow it.

Male and Female Red Pill Case Offenders Heavily Sentenced; Heaviest Sentence is Ten Years and a Fine; Wang Xiuying Cried Loudly Upon Hearing the Verdict 98

The Lou Jia Wan Central Police Station of the French Concession, at noon on the 24th of last month, received a report from the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau and was led by Western detective Bi Ye, along with Chinese detectives Wang Zhihao, Peng Zhengyou, Li Baochang, Yang Weishan, and others, first went to No. 12 Rihui Lane, Jin Shenfu Road, and arrested Yuan Hongsheng, Wang Tugeng, Zhang Dehui, and three other suspects who were selling morphine and red pills. Forty-five small bags of morphine and twenty-five small bags of red pills were seized and taken to the police station. Based on Yuan's confession, they first went to No. 569 Fada Road and arrested Jiang Yongmei, who was wholesaling morphine, and then went to No. 9 Songbai Lane, Liumei Road, and continued to arrest the woman Cao Wangshi and the suspect Wang Jinwu. A bag of morphine weighing about two taels was found behind the back wall of the closet in the rear building, as well as more than seventy yuan in cash from sales. Then, they went to No. 10, Lane 150, Fuxu Road, and arrested Zhang Genxing, who was wholesaling red pills. They then went to the rear building of No. 59, Jule Road, and continued to arrest the young woman Wang Xiuying and the man Yin Peiben, a couple, and found eight bags of red pills, totaling 8,000 pills, under the floor of the rear building, as well as a full set of equipment for manufacturing red pills, and a wooden box with a concealed bottom and a white leather box for transporting the pills. A total of nine male and female criminals were arrested in five places, along with the stolen goods, and taken back to the police station and sent to the Special Second Court for questioning and detention. It was found that Cao Wangshi, Wang Xiuying, and others had also committed similar cases before and had been punished on record. However, no criminal suspicion was found against Zhang Dehui. The day before yesterday afternoon, Judge Xiong Huiping of the Special Second Court opened a court session for interrogation. The police lawyer did not prosecute Zhang Dehui, and the remaining defendants were prosecuted in accordance with Article 257 of the Criminal Law for selling and manufacturing opium compounds. The Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau sent personnel to the case and requested permission to transfer Yuan Hongsheng, Wang Tugeng, and Zhang Dehui, three criminals. After the court thoroughly interrogated the defendants and declared the debate closed, a date was set for sentencing. The details of the case related to the transfer request of the Public Security Bureau will be announced at the time of sentencing. This has been reported in detail in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, Judge Xiong came to the Third Criminal Court and ordered the defendants to be brought to the case. After briefly questioning their ages and places of origin, the judgment was announced (details of the crimes omitted). Yin Peiben was sentenced to ten years' imprisonment and fined 1,500 yuan. Cao Wangshi was sentenced to ten years' imprisonment and fined 1,000 yuan. Wang Xiuying was sentenced to eight years' imprisonment and fined 500 yuan. Zhang Genxing was sentenced to four years' imprisonment and fined 200 yuan. Jiang Yongmei was sentenced to four years' imprisonment. Yuan Hongsheng was sentenced to six years' imprisonment. Wang Tugeng was sentenced to three months' imprisonment for smoking opium compounds. Wang Jinwu was found not guilty. If fines are commuted to labor, Yin Peiben, Cao Wangshi, and Wang Xiuying will be calculated on the basis of the total amount and the number of days in six months, and Zhang Genxing will be calculated at three yuan per day. The seized morphine, red pill equipment, and other items were confiscated and burned. Zhang Dehui was released on bail after completing the necessary procedures and passing the appeal period. Yuan Hongsheng, Wang Tugeng, and Zhang Dehui do not need to be transferred to the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau. During the appeal period, the defendants were all transferred to the detention center. When Wang Xiuying, one of the defendants, heard that she was sentenced to eight years in prison, she burst into tears and cried out "Mother!" It can be seen that the law is strict. Although she repents and cries now, it is too late. The defendants all whispered that they could only appeal for relief in the hope of a reduced sentence. When they were led down by the bailiffs and returned to the detention center, the defendants all had tears in their eyes and bowed their heads as they entered the detention center.

United Company Purchased New Funing Steamer; Starting on the 4th, It Will Operate on the Shanghai-Funing Route 99

Since the China United Wharf Warehouse Company opened the Shanghai-Funing route, it has purchased the Fuping steamer and renamed it Funing. The repairs have been completed, and the maiden voyage to Funing is approved for the 4th. The details are as follows:

Purchased the Fuping Steamer. The Fuping steamer of the Zhenxing Steamship Company was formerly represented by Zhen'an Management Steamship Company. It has now been purchased by the United Company, and the repairs have been completed. The total tonnage of the vessel is 1,202 tons, the net tonnage is 654 tons, the length is 230 feet 4 inches, the width is 31 feet 2 inches, the depth is 15 feet 5 inches, the draft is 150 feet, the horsepower is 104, and the speed is 10 nautical miles per hour. It was built in 1912 and has now been renamed Funing.

Sailing to Funing. The company announced yesterday: "In order to make passenger and cargo transportation in the Huainan area faster and more convenient, in addition to the original Muyou steamer, we have added a new Funing steamer to operate between Shanghai, Funing, and Menglong. There will be three scheduled trips per month. The cabins are comfortable and the fares are low, divided into first, second, and third classes, with a capacity of more than 200 passengers. The journey is fast, reaching Funing in 40 hours and Menglong in 45 hours. Passenger and cargo transportation is extremely fast. Your patronage is welcome. Address: Wangjia Wharf, Nanshi, Shanghai. Telephone: 21493 (roundabout). The ship docks at Wharf No. 17, Nanshi."

Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway to Manage Passenger Car Tea and Water Themselves; Cancellation of Merchant-Operated Contracts Scheduled to Take Effect Today 100

Since the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway Bureau took over the management of passenger car tea and water, the results have been good and there has been a surplus. The Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway passenger cars have been operated by merchants under contract. Since they are not satisfied with the current arrangement, the Traffic Department has requested and been approved by the Railway Bureau to take it back and manage it themselves, following the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway model, starting on December 1st.

Low-Pressure System Arrived; It Was Drizzling in Shanghai Yesterday 101

Huadong News Agency reported that the city has been overcast and rainy for days. Yesterday, due to a low-pressure system arriving from Jiujiang, the drizzle was even heavier. Around 11:00 AM and 2:00 PM, the rain was like hailstones (at this time, the air pressure was at 28 degrees north latitude and 115 degrees east longitude, near the south side of Shanghai, which made the rain even heavier). By 4:00 PM, the raindrops had stopped. Last night, the low-pressure system was between 31 degrees north latitude and 121 degrees east longitude, causing heavy rain in various ports along the Yangtze River. The entry and exit of planes and ships were obstructed.
