Rickshaw Pullers Most Afraid of Nails and Glass on the Road; Mutual Aid Society Appeals to Citizens Not to Litter 106

The Shanghai Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Society has recently received claims from members such as Qiu Shigui and Wu Shan, stating that they were injured by nails and glass shards thrown on the road, and requested assistance. The association has provided medical treatment and food rations to each of them. It has been found that 60% to 70% of these injured rickshaw pullers have family burdens, with elderly parents and young children. Pulling a rickshaw is their only means of livelihood, and their feet are important tools. Now that they are unable to walk, without the relief offered by the association, those waiting to be fed will face starvation. Compatriots, who does not have parents, who does not have children? Compassion is inherent in all people. It is hoped that citizens of this city will pay attention to this in the future and intervene and stop such behavior at any time, benefiting laborers. The merits are immeasurable.

Railway Bureau Adds Through Transport from Shanghai North to Kouan 107

The two railways and the Xicheng Long-Distance Bus Company have long been handling through transport of passengers, luggage, and parcels. The company stipulates that Tangtouqiao, Yanqiao, Qingyang, Nanzha, Jiangyin, and other five locations are the connecting stations, and Wuxi is the connecting station for both parties. Now, the company considers Kouan to be a major hub along the river, with thousands of merchants entering and leaving every day, and requests that the through transport line be extended to Kouan to facilitate travel. The Railway Bureau has agreed to add through transport from Shanghai North Station to Kouan. All measures will continue to be handled according to the previously agreed contract. The section of the road from Jiangyin to Kouan will be operated by a specially contracted shipping company, and the fees will be borne by the company. The ticket prices and other items between Shanghai North and Kouan have been agreed upon by both parties.

Accountants Association: Minutes of the Meeting of the Building Association Hall Committee 108

The Building Association Hall Committee of the Accountants Association held its 16th committee meeting yesterday. Committee members Tang Zaizhang, Wang Zikang, Qin Kai, Xi Yushu, Wang Haifan, Jiang Wanping, Bei Zuyi, Xie Lin, Pan Xulun, and Li Wenjie attended. Member Chen Riping was present as a non-voting attendee. Jiang Wanping was elected chairman, and Li Wenjie served as the secretary. (A) Report items: (1) The autumn general meeting of members passed three principles regarding the committee's proposal to build the association's hall: 1. Considering the association's financial strength, according to the previous resolution of the members' meeting, select a suitable location of about two mu in the city center to build the hall. The design should be simple and practical, and a ledger storage room should be built on the lower floor of the building to store ledgers entrusted to the members for safekeeping. The total cost of land purchase, construction, and equipment should not exceed 30,000 yuan. 2. The existing building association hall fund has a fixed deposit of 19,000 yuan in the bank, a current deposit of more than 500 yuan, and the association's fund (amounting to 6,000 yuan) can all be used for building the hall. If it is not enough, members should find ways to raise donations, and membership fees should not be pre-collected. 3. In addition to the original seven committee members, the standing directors of the association will be added as committee members for building the hall. (2) Soliciting suitable land in the city center. Applicants include five locations: Minfu Road, Sanmin Road, Guoguang Road, Zhengyi Road, and Xiangyin Road. (B) Matters for discussion: (1) Land purchase case. It was resolved that the land price should be limited to 13,000 yuan. Xie Lin, Jiang Wanping, and Li Wenjie were appointed to conduct an on-site inspection of the land on Guoguang Road and Xiangyin Road and make a decision immediately. (2) How to withdraw the bank's fixed deposit. It was resolved that Member Bei Zuyi should go to the bank to contact and handle the matter. (3) The case of entrusting the building association hall fund to staff for safekeeping. It was resolved that the original seven committee members should continue to be entrusted with safekeeping to facilitate the replacement of seals. (4) After the construction of the association hall begins, the expenditure of funds will be frequent. Should a current account with check usage be opened at the bank? It was resolved that a check current account and checkbook should be opened at the Bank of China, and Member Li Wenjie should be entrusted with safekeeping. (5) How to handle the architectural design of the association hall? It was resolved that Xie Lin, Wang Haifan, and Wang Zikang should be responsible for handling the matter. The meeting adjourned.

Third Branch of the Citizen Association Discusses Double Taxation of Road Construction Beyond Boundaries; Requests Approval from the General Federation of Citizen Associations 109

In Xiaoshadu and Caojiadu in West Shanghai, electricity, telephone, and tap water on roads constructed beyond the boundaries are supplied by the Public Concession. After the Xinhai Revolution, the Public Works Department charged residents and businesses in that area who used water, electricity, and telephones an extraterritorial municipal tax (i.e., patrol tax), with a tax rate lower than that within the boundaries by 2%. It initially levied 12% and then 14%. Since the city government began levying a municipal general tax (i.e., house tax), the citizens in that area have not paid the city tax because they cannot bear the double taxation and cannot avoid using the water and electricity of the concession. Later, negotiations were held to recover the roads beyond the boundaries, so the matter was put on hold. Recently, the Shanghai West Electricity Company was established, and the city government granted a business license. There is no longer a problem with using electricity. The citizens in that area then raised the issue of paying the concession patrol tax at the general meeting of the third branch of the Citizen Association. Should the payment be stopped at this time, or should the original situation be maintained? After repeated discussions, it was resolved to submit the matter to the General Federation of Citizen Associations for instructions.

Female Teacher Wang Quanquying Threatened; Search for Letter Paper and Handwriting as Evidence; Liang Linzhang Confesses that Ni Guoxiang Initiated It; Police Detective Work is Swift and Appraisal is Required 110

Wang Quanquying, a female teacher at Nanjing Jinling University, is from Ningbo, Zhejiang. Her home address is No. 54 Hengde Lane, Hart Road, Shanghai Public Concession. At about 8:00 AM on November 27th, Ms. Wang suddenly found a letter on the floor in the kitchen. It was addressed to the honorable owner of No. 54. Upon inspection, it turned out to be a threatening letter. The signatory was the bandit leader Yao Houhuo, who stated that he had more than a dozen bandits under his command and was now extorting 5,000 yuan from the honorable owner. He asked her to meet him in front of Sincere Company. If she saw someone wearing blue cloth pants, she could contact him. If she did not agree, they would come to rob her or murder her family. He also stated that the representative they sent was carrying a handgun, etc. Ms. Wang reported the letter to the Gordon Road Police Station in charge. Hua Detective Zhu Mengwei, Detective Gao Huixian, He Renrui, and others were assigned to investigate, and they took turns guarding Ms. Wang's home to prevent accidents. On the morning of the 28th, Detective Gao Huixian was waiting at Wang's house when he suddenly heard a slight noise in the kitchen. He went to check and found another letter had been thrown in. Detective Gao quickly went out the back door and saw a man in a suit standing in the nearby lane. There was no one else suspicious. Detective Gao stepped forward and asked him. The man stammered and said his name was Liang Linzhang, from Guangdong, and lived at No. 62 Hengde Lane. The detectives went to No. 62 to check and found that the man did live there. At that time, there was no evidence, so he was not arrested. He reported back to the police station and conducted further investigation. It was discovered that Liang Linzhang was a relative of Mr. Liang, a Cantonese resident of No. 62, and was unemployed. However, he was highly suspected in this case, so he was arrested on the day. With the permission of his relative Mr. Liang, the detectives searched his room and found several sheets of paper (the same as the paper in the letter received by Ms. Wang). He was taken to the police station. Under questioning, he admitted everything and confessed that Ni Guoxiang, a servant of Zhang Yougu (an employee of the Shanghai Electric Power Company located at No. 60 in the lane), was also an accomplice. Chinese and Western detectives then went to arrest Ni and found an ink brush, ink, and a sheet of paper. They were taken back to the police station and detained. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special Court and prosecuted for attempted extortion under Article 346, Paragraph 3 of the Criminal Law. The police lawyer Zhang Tianyin then rose to state the case, saying that the victim Wang Quanquying had received two letters in total, the first demanding 5,000 yuan and the second reduced to 3,000 yuan. After the two defendants were arrested, Liang Linzhang was asked to write a note in the police station. His handwriting was the same as the letters received by Ms. Wang, and the English date written on the back of the original letter also matched the English written by Liang. Because the handwriting has not yet been appraised by experts, and there is also a resident surnamed Li in Hengde Lane where the plaintiff lives who has also received a threatening letter, he requested that the trial be postponed. Wang Quanquying then filed a complaint, recounting what happened. Under questioning, Liang Linzhang confessed that Ni Guoxiang initiated the matter. Ni's nickname is A-huo, so Yao Houhuo is Ni's alias. Ni drafted the letter and asked me to copy it. If he got 5,000 yuan, I could get 500 yuan. Ni Guoxiang denied everything. Judge Liu Yugui reviewed the confession and ordered the two defendants to be detained for seven days before the next hearing.

It is truly a good opportunity to achieve two goals at once.

Someone Reports Secretly; Drug Dealer Yang Zhushi and Others Arrested; Three People Sleeping on the Same Bed Smoking Opium; Police Find Drug Gun Thrown Out of the Window Based on Anonymous Tip 117

The Yimiao Police Station received an anonymous report from Gu Bingkui the night before, stating that there was a secret organization selling red pills (opium pills) for lamp smoking in No. 2 Zhangjia Lane, Xiaotianzhu Lane, in the city. The lane is small and winding, very secretive, and a detailed diagram was attached. Director Liu, upon receiving the report, immediately ordered the household registration inspector Chen Shusheng to lead the police to rush to the scene. They found the door according to the diagram and went straight up to the upper floor. They saw Yang Zhushi (39 years old, from Shanghai), Yang Xingxing (34 years old, same), and Shao Xuede (47 years old) sleeping on the same bed, smoking opium pills. They were immediately arrested, and three opium pill guns, one opium pipe, one lamp, three bags of opium pills (44 pills), more than ten empty bags of opium pills, one can of opium pill ash, and a small amount of opium paste and ash were found. While searching for other evidence, Yang Zhushi, in order to destroy the evidence, took the opportunity to throw the three opium pill guns out of the window, causing the magnetic heads to break. The evidence was taken to the police station for investigation. After Director Liu questioned him, Yang Zhushi confessed that the opium pills were bought from the entrance of Yinhe Lane in the French Concession. The case is related to the enforced ban on drugs and opium. It is planned to send the case to the general bureau for strict handling.

Barber Teases and Injures Passing Women; Tian Jinrong Fined 100 Yuan 118

Yang Pangshi, a woman from Nanxiang, named Jinmei, who lives at No. 86 Wenzhou Road, goes out to shop every day. When she passes the Overseas Chinese Barber Shop at No. 352 Avenue Edward VII, the barber in the shop often utters dirty words and teases her. Because she could not reason with them, she did not argue with them. At 9:40 AM the day before yesterday, she was walking with her cousin Wu Xiaomao when Tian Jinrong, the manager of the shop from Yangzhou, and the barber Bai Henglin said that her buttocks were well-developed and lovely, and that she could raise sparrows on her buttocks, and that if she had money, she could buy them. Wu Xiaomao stepped forward to question them, but Tian and others not only did not repent but dragged the siblings into the shop. Tian then used a razor to cut the woman's head. Wu Xiaomao saw this and immediately stopped him with his hand, causing his palm to be injured by the knife. Wu and the woman grabbed Tian and went to the Xinzha Police Station. Hua Detective Yang Youshan investigated and found that it was true and took Tian into custody. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special Court. Police Lawyer Qian Xunjiu prosecuted him for intentional injury under Article 277, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law and requested that he be severely punished according to the law. Yang Pangshi and others then submitted a report on the situation at that time. The defendant confessed that the plaintiff had invited many people to come and cause trouble, that the injury was not caused by him, and that there was no teasing. Judge Dai Rongduo reviewed the confession and sentenced Tian to a fine of 100 yuan. If he chose to perform labor service instead, it would be calculated at one yuan per day. During the appeal period, he had to submit a guarantee deposit or a guarantee letter of the same amount.

Heavy Exploitation: Tai Feng Pawnshop Accused; Wei Duanmin Files Private Prosecution, Zhang Yongjia Admits Interest 119

The current criminal law stipulates that the exploitation of excessive interest is a crime, and ordinary small pawnshops are the first to bear the brunt. In recent months, complaints from those who have pawned items have become commonplace. Now, Tai Feng Pawnshop at 1272 Labor Sheng Road has also been accused of exploiting excessive interest by Wei Duanmin from Yancheng, who has filed a criminal private prosecution with the First Special District Court. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu Zehan held a court hearing. According to Wei's statement, he was studying at China Public School and needed money on July 23rd. He asked Tang San to pawn an electric fan at the pawnshop for seven yuan. However, the pawn ticket stated seven yuan, seven jiao, and one fen, and the redemption period was shortened from August to April. When he went to redeem the item on the 23rd of this month, he paid a total of eight yuan, three jiao, one fen, and six li for principal and interest. This means that the monthly interest rate was actually as high as four fen and seven li, which is undoubtedly exploitation of excessive interest. Zhang Yongjia, the manager of the accused Tai Feng Pawnshop, stated that the pawn amount paid to Tang San for the electric fan was seven yuan in silver dollars and eight jiao in small coins, plus one jiao for the storage of the pawned item. Therefore, the pawn ticket stated seven yuan, seven jiao, and one fen. Because the electric fan was made of iron and easily damaged, the pawning period was shortened from August to April. All of this was agreed upon face-to-face with the pawner. Later, when the plaintiff came to redeem the item, interest was calculated at two fen per month, so he charged a total of eight yuan, three jiao, one fen, and six li for principal and interest, of which six jiao and eight li were interest. Furthermore, around the 18th or 19th of this month, someone came to the store and said that someone would sue me, but I didn't pay attention to it at first. Unexpectedly, this morning, two people named Liu and Ding came to the store and said that they were familiar with Wei and were willing to mediate, asking me to spend a little money to settle the matter, but I didn't agree. He also submitted the pawnshop's pawned item ledger as evidence. Tang San then testified in court, saying that he only received seven yuan for the pawn, and the money and pawn ticket were handed over to Wei's wife. Wei continued to say that he was ill that day and only knew the amount on the pawn ticket was different from the actual amount paid by the pawnshop when he went to redeem the item. Judge Wu then adjourned the hearing to December 7th in the afternoon for further questioning.

Transfer of Yang Peter Issue: Temporary Detention During Appeal Period 120

Yang Peter, a native of Xinhui and an employee of the Hong Kong branch of the Guangdong Bank, embezzled more than 198,000 yuan in August of the year before last and fled to Shanghai, hiding with his concubine Wang Baoqiong in the Delin Apartment on Chongming Road. Recently, the bank found out about it, telegraphed the Hongkou Police Station, sent detectives to arrest him, and handed him over to the First Special District Court for detention pending investigation, as reported in previous newspapers. It is now learned that after Yang was arrested, the branch reported to the head office, which in turn asked the Guangdong Provincial Government to telegraph the Shanghai Municipal Government to negotiate with the Public Works Bureau for extradition. Mayor Wu ordered Cai, the director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, to send a letter and specially assign detectives to submit it to the First Special Court yesterday morning, requesting permission to transfer the suspect to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for detention, so that the Guangdong provincial authorities could come to escort him. Judge Xiao Xiechen held a court hearing and ordered Yang to be brought up for questioning. Yang's lawyer, Jiang Yiping, argued that the Guangdong Provincial Government telegraphed the Municipal Government to request negotiations with the Public Works Bureau, but Director Cai of the Public Security Bureau requested the transfer from the court, which is inconsistent with the procedure. First, the Public Security Bureau is also detaining him while waiting for Guangdong to escort him, which is no different from detaining him in the court while waiting for Guangdong to come. Second, since Guangdong wants to transfer him, why not have the local court prepare a document to request the transfer, but now it is being handled by a non-judicial organization. Third, therefore, he still requests that Yang be detained and proceed according to law. However, the representative of the Public Security Bureau stated in court that the transfer procedures were complete. Zhang Shizhu, a lawyer from the Public Works Bureau, also stated that the Public Works Bureau had no opinion on the transfer and asked the court to handle it. Judge Xiao then ordered Yang Peter to be taken away by the personnel from the Municipal Public Security Bureau. Lawyer Jiang Yiping immediately declared an appeal on behalf of Yang, requesting that the transfer not be carried out during the appeal period, and cited the precedent of the Third Branch of the High Court revoking the Second Special Court's approval of the transfer by non-judicial organs in the mainland, arguing for a long time. Judge Xiao then replied, "Temporary detention during the appeal period." Thus, Yang Peter was still taken back to the police station for detention.

Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau Announces Simple Life Insurance Regulations (Continued) 123

Payment of Premiums: Chapter 3. Payment of Premiums. Article 16. Premiums shall be paid monthly. The date stated on the insurance policy shall be the due date of the insurance. The premium due shall be paid within one month. Article 17. Premiums may be paid in advance. If the insured wishes to pay the premiums for every six months at once, they may enjoy a discount equal to half a month's premium. If they pay for twelve months at once, they may enjoy a discount equal to one month's premium. According to the provisions of the preceding paragraph, if the policyholder pays the premium in advance without deducting the discount amount, the Insurance Bureau shall return the discount portion to the policyholder. Article 18. Premiums shall be paid to the Insurance Bureau or premium collector designated at the time of the contract. After receiving the premium, the Insurance Bureau or premium collector shall immediately register it on the insurance receipt. Those who continuously pay premiums to the Insurance Bureau for twelve months (excluding supplementary premium payments) may enjoy a discount equal to half a month's premium. Article 19. If a premium is paid to a collector, and payment is repeatedly delayed, the Insurance Bureau may order them to pay to the Bureau. Article 20. If the same policyholder has one or more insurance contracts, they may request a pre-determined date to pay the premiums for each contract simultaneously. However, all unpaid premiums for each contract must be paid in full. Article 21. When requesting combined payment according to the provisions of the preceding article, the policyholder shall first declare the date, method, and location of payment. The date in the preceding paragraph shall be the same as the date prescribed in Article 16. Article 22. When a policyholder requests combined payment according to the provisions of Article 20, they shall fill out an application form in the prescribed format and deliver it to the Insurance Bureau along with the premium receipt. Once the request in the preceding paragraph is approved, a new premium receipt shall be issued and delivered to the policyholder. Article 23. When a policyholder requests to stop combined payment for all or part of the premium, they shall fill out an application form in the prescribed format and deliver it to the Insurance Bureau along with the premium receipt. Once the Insurance Bureau approves the request in the preceding paragraph, or if there is a change in the amount of combined premium payments, a new premium receipt shall be issued. Article 24. When a policyholder enters into a second insurance contract, the payment date for the premium may be applied mutatis mutandis to the provisions of Articles 20 and 22, and the premium receipt for the first contract shall be delivered to the Insurance Bureau along with the application for the second contract, requesting combined payment of the premium, without the need for a separate application form. Article 25. When a policyholder requests to change the payment location, they shall fill out an application form in the prescribed format and deliver it to the original insurance bureau for transfer to the Postal Reserve Gold Exchange Bureau for verification. Article 26. The grace period for premium payment shall be two months, calculated from the first day after the date prescribed in Article 16 expires. During the grace period, a supplementary premium payment shall be 1% of the premium due, with any amount less than one yuan calculated as one yuan. Article 27. If the insured suffers an accident after the insurance contract becomes effective, resulting in the loss of both hands or both feet, or one hand and one foot, or blindness in both eyes, and wishes to continue the contract, they may request mid-term disability exemption from premium payments. Article 28. The request in the preceding article shall be made by the policyholder filling out an application form in the prescribed format, along with a doctor's diagnosis certificate and other supporting documents, and the insurance policy, all of which shall be delivered to the Insurance Bureau. Article 29. If the Insurance Bureau approves the request in Article 27, it shall note the reason for the premium exemption and the effective date on the insurance policy and return the original insurance policy. The policyholder is exempt from paying the premiums due thereafter.

Insurance Amount: Chapter 4. Payment of Insurance Amount. Article 30. In the event of the death of the insured, the policyholder or beneficiary shall immediately report to the Insurance Bureau, and the Bureau shall send someone to verify. If the policyholder or beneficiary fails to report the death of the insured immediately, making it impossible for the Insurance Bureau to verify, they shall provide a guarantee to prove the death of the insured when requesting payment of the insurance amount. Article 31. When paying the insurance amount, if there are any of the following outstanding debts that have not been cleared, they shall be deducted from the payment amount: (1) Premiums and late fees that have been delayed; (2) Principal and interest on loans. Article 32. When a beneficiary requests payment of the insurance amount, they shall fill out an application form in the prescribed format and deliver it to the Insurance Bureau along with the insurance policy and premium receipt. When requesting payment of the insurance amount due to the death of the insured, a doctor's diagnosis certificate and other supporting documents shall be attached. Article 33. If the Insurance Bureau deems the request in the preceding article to be legal upon receipt, it shall immediately fill out a payment voucher according to the insurance amount and deliver it to the beneficiary. Upon receiving the payment voucher, the beneficiary shall sign and stamp it in the prescribed format and take it to the bureau specified on the voucher along with the receipt from the insurance policy to collect the insurance money. Article 34. If the beneficiary requests to change the location of insurance amount collection to a bureau other than the one specified, they shall pay remittance fees according to postal regulations. (To be continued)

The 93rd Inspection Report of the Shanghai Bank of China Issuance Preparation Inspection Committee states that, based on the rules, the committee inspected the special reserve vault for the issuance and borrowing of exchange coupons by the Shanghai Bank of China and its affiliated banks and merchants. On November 24th, 1935, Xu Kan, Director of the Currency Department of the Ministry of Finance, Wang Yansong and Pei Yunqing, representatives of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, Zhang Peishen and Hu Xian, representatives of the Shanghai Banking Association, Liu Wuqiao and Zhang Wenbo, representatives of the Shanghai Money Dealers Association, Qi Yunqing and Lin Rongsheng, representatives of the coupon-issuing merchants, and Zhou Zongliang, Wang Baolun, and Lu Jianquan, representatives of the directors and supervisors of the bank, together with accountant Wang Zikang, conducted the 93rd inspection at the bank. The total amount of exchange coupon reserves is 247,600,5851 yuan, including 90,240,167.3 yuan in cash reserves and 57,365,683.7 yuan in guarantee reserves. Letter Received:

Respectfully,

We have just received a telegram from the captain of our company's Changxing ship stating, "The Shen Bao newspaper on the 29th reported that our ship ran aground and the engine room flooded. Where did this news come from? We are deeply shocked and hope you will send a letter to correct it, to avoid misunderstandings among passengers' families and cargo owners."

After investigation, we have found that your newspaper did indeed publish such a report on the 29th, which is indeed misleading. Furthermore, the ship safely escaped danger last night during the high tide and is sailing as usual, without any damage to the hull. Grounding during periods of low water is a common occurrence. We are writing to urgently request that you investigate and correct the report to rectify the facts and avoid misunderstandings. We would be most grateful for your public service.

Sincerely,

Li Zhiyi

November 30, 1935

Sports News

National Football Association:

Explains Important Questions Regarding Rules

Published by the Chinese National Amateur Athletic Federation

The Chinese National Amateur Athletic Federation has received a copy of the minutes from the meeting of the International Football Association Rules and Referees Committee held in Paris on October 5th. The minutes contain several examples of questions and answers regarding the interpretation of the rules. We are now publishing these for adoption by the football community.

(1) Interpretation of Rules

Chapter 10: Free Kicks

(Question) A player takes a free kick under Chapter 10, and before the ball is touched by another player, that player (i.e., the kicker) commits a handball. If a player commits two violations, how should the referee rule?

(Answer) The referee should choose the more serious of the two violations and penalize it.

Chapter 16: Restarting After a Temporary Suspension

(Question) When the referee drops the ball, and before the ball touches the ground, a player commits a handball. How should the referee rule?

(Answer) The referee should award a free kick for the handball.

The committee suggests that referees should only apply the above two decisions when the player's violation is very obvious.

(2) The Authority of the Referee and its Relation to the Start of the Match

The committee reaffirms the 1932 resolution that the referee's authority in the field of play, as stipulated by regulations, should begin after the whistle is blown. If a player violates the rules after the whistle is blown, they can be ordered off the field and not replaced. However, to prevent practical difficulties, national football associations should grant referees sufficient administrative authority to determine that the referee's authority begins before the match starts.

(3) Questions Regarding Rules

(Question) Attacking player A advances into the opponent's penalty area and attempts to pass the ball to the center, but the ball crosses the goal line while remaining in play. At that moment, defending player B, standing on the goal line, commits a violation of Rule 9 against player A. How should the referee rule?

(Answer) The referee should award a penalty kick.

(Question) Suppose someone in the audience blows a whistle, causing the match to stop suddenly. How should the referee handle this?

(Answer) The referee can be lenient in such situations, as players stopping upon hearing a whistle is a sign of good sportsmanship and obedience. The match should be restarted with a dropped ball.

Meng Ruier to Arrive in Shanghai Tomorrow

Performance at the China Tennis Club at 1:30 PM. Tickets: $1 or $2. If it rains, moved to the Shen Yuan Basketball Court.

Czech Davis Cup players Meng Ruier and Ha Tuo are currently touring the Far East. Inspector Zhong of the Ministry of Education Inspects Zhejiang Province Vocational Education Report (5):

18. Private Guanghua Junior High School Commerce Program and Private Sanyu Junior Commercial School:

The private Guanghua Junior High School Commerce Program has three classes with over 80 students. In order to provide practical training and career opportunities for the first graduating class next year, the school is in contact with various banks and financial institutions in Hangzhou in the hopes of securing service opportunities for some of its students. The school's on-site training facilities are adequate, typing is good, but banking and commerce facilities are poor. To accommodate the demands of a small number of students' parents, the school offers preparatory courses for higher education from the second year onwards, while exempting students from the core commerce subjects. This approach is not appropriate. Such supplementary classes should only be conducted outside of regular class hours. The school's advertising efforts are noteworthy, but the results are ordinary. The private Sanyu Junior Commercial School has three junior classes and three vocational training classes, with a total of 110 students. The curriculum distribution is appropriate. Banking practice consists of only five or six visits to local banks upon graduation. The store has a basic structure, but there is too little business and no opportunity for practice. Most students choose to pursue higher education, with fewer entering the workforce directly. The typing training program is well-managed. The school's geography and English teaching methods and materials are inadequate. The school has a noticeable Christian atmosphere. The faculty in each department needs improvement. The school should offer more vocational training classes and reduce the number of junior commerce classes to better reflect the actual needs.

19. Private Commercial Society Commercial Training School:

The school offers two departments: general and specialized. The general department offers 12 hours of instruction per week, while the specialized department focuses on electives. It offers four specializations: accounting, banking, English, and Japanese. Each student must choose two specializations, with each specialization meeting for three to four hours per week. Most students are employees of banks, money shops, and stores. Their classroom performance is good. The curriculum distribution is appropriate. Most of the teachers are also instructors at commercial vocational schools. (End)

Children's Educational Novel

Little Men (111) 131

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, Translated by Zheng Xiaocang

They were very happy that afternoon, although there were quite a few mishaps, which are common in such long journeys! Of course, Tommo caused trouble again. He fell on a hornet's nest and was stung fiercely by them, but he was used to such hardships and was able to endure them until Nan suggested using some wet mud, which reduced his pain considerably. Daisy saw a snake and immediately ran away, spilling half of her wild strawberries. Later, Demi helped her refill her basket, while discussing reptiles with his vast knowledge. Nat fell out of a tree, tearing the back of his vest completely, but fortunately there were no other tears. As and Jack were arguing over a particularly lush spot, just as they reached a stalemate, Tommy quietly and quickly swept everything away, hurrying to Dan's side for protection. At that time, Dan was also very happy, his crutches had been discarded, and he was wandering freely in the prairie, very comfortable, unaware that there was so much strength in his legs. He saw interesting rocks and roots scattered across the prairie, many familiar small animals crawling in the grass, and many insects dancing in the air.

But the most thrilling thing that afternoon was what happened to Nan and Rob. This event later became a family anecdote that was often talked about at the Plumfield, and was still talked about with great interest after a long time. Nan had explored the area, tearing her coat in three places and scratching her face on a thorn bush, and then began picking strawberries, which were bright, shiny, and black, like large beads, on the low green bushes. Her nimble fingers were flying over them, but her basket was not easily filled, so she searched east and west for better places, unlike Daisy, who was content to pick quietly. Rob followed Nan, because her vigorous spirit suited his temperament better than his cousin's patient work, and he was also eager to pick the biggest and best strawberries for "Marmee".

Ministry of Education Approves Imprint of Three Principles of the People Thousand Character Primer 132

The Ministry of Education's A, B, and C types of Thousand Character Primers have been widely adopted by various provinces and cities. Recently, the Education Bureaus of Jiangyin, Nanhui, Xiaoxian, Yixing, Jiading, and Chuansha counties in Jiangsu Province requested the Shanghai Beixin Bookstore to imprint hundreds of thousands of copies of the C type primer. This has been submitted by the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education to the Ministry of Education for approval. According to the person in charge of the relevant department of the Ministry of Education, the Ministry has always welcomed the imprint of this primer by all sectors. In addition to having samples available for reference, there are also measures for imprinting the Three Principles of the People Thousand Character Primer, which were announced in March of the 20th year and published in the 11th issue of the 3rd volume of the Ministry's gazette and the compilation of educational laws. Anyone wishing to imprint the primer only needs to submit a sample to the Ministry for approval in accordance with these measures, and they can then be printed and sold. There is no exclusive sale by anyone, and the Ministry has never approved any individual or bookstore to have exclusive sales rights. Recently, the Datong Bookstore suddenly published an advertisement in the Shanghai Xin Shen newspapers regarding the imprint and sale of the Three Principles of the People Thousand Character Primer. The Ministry considered this to be close to a monopoly and has strictly prohibited it. Before printing, the sample must be submitted to the Ministry for approval, which is done to prevent shoddy printing, errors, and excessively high prices.

Shuangqiu Invents Popular Education Vehicle to be Demonstrated in Beijing; Submission for Ministry of Industry Award to Manufacture and Distribute in Shanghai 133

(Central News Agency, Nanjing, 30th) Tai Shuangqiu's invented Popular Education Vehicle will be publicly demonstrated to the press and education sectors in Beijing on the 1st. The vehicle has a unique structure. The exterior is a rectangular wooden box with three wheels at the bottom that can be pushed to various locations. The front and rear panels of the vehicle can be flipped up to serve as blackboards and laid flat to become long tables for exhibitions and ping-pong games. The vehicle also has iron frames for erecting canopies and hanging blackboards, charts, books, abacuses, and other items. The vehicle is equipped with five pairs of Active Popular Education Boxes, which contain various educational supplies. It is truly a useful tool for promoting popular education. Tai has submitted a request to the Ministry of Industry for an award and plans to manufacture and distribute the vehicle in Shanghai.

China Social Education Society: Preparations for the Fourth Annual Meeting Nearing Completion; Meeting Advanced by Three Days, to Begin on January 18th 136

The China Social Education Society is the only social education academic organization in our country. Its annual meetings have made great contributions to social education academics in our country. The society's fourth annual meeting was originally scheduled to be held at Sun Yat-sen University in Guangzhou starting on January 21st of next year. Recently, a telegram was received from the Guangzhou Preparatory Committee stating that, as the time coincides with the Lunar New Year, according to Southern customs, all businesses and printing workers will be closed as usual. This would cause inconvenience for the progress of the annual meeting and for the travel of society members. Therefore, it was decided to advance the meeting by three days, holding it from January 18th to 22nd. The society has already issued an urgent notice to all society members attending the meeting. Furthermore, National Sun Yat-sen University believes that the society's annual meeting in Guangzhou will definitely provide much guidance for social education in South China. Therefore, it is providing a subsidy of 4,000 national currency for society members to attend. The deadline for society members to register for attendance has now passed. In addition to the Guangzhou society members, a total of 254 people have registered. Social education experts Liang Shuming, Jiang Jianyu, Gao Jiansi, Meng Xiancheng, Jin Lingxiu, Zhao Buxia, Yu Qingtang, Li Zheng, and Chen Jianzhao will all attend on schedule. Zhang Jiong, Director of the Social Education Department of the Ministry of Education, has also notified the society that he has decided to attend. Recently, Xiao Guanying, Cui Zaiyang, and other members of the society's annual meeting preparatory committee have been actively preparing, sparing no effort, it is said.

Wu Yan-yin of the Ministry of Education Has Been Inspecting Schools in Shanghai for Two Weeks 137

Wu Yan-yin, Section Chief of the Ministry of Education, has been in Shanghai inspecting primary and secondary schools for two weeks. He has inspected more than 40 schools. At each school, he provides detailed guidance. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, a discussion meeting was held at the Municipal Education Bureau with section chiefs, supervisors, and inspectors to discuss Shanghai's education issues in great detail. Furthermore, Mr. Wu went to Pudong the day before yesterday to inspect the Municipal Xinlu Normal School. He conducted a detailed inspection of the school's administration, teaching, and discipline in all aspects, and found that it was well managed. He especially praised the school's work-study course equipment and teaching. In the afternoon, he delivered a speech to all the teachers and students of the school, presenting the two points of advancement and in-depth study to encourage them. The speech lasted for an hour, it is said.

Commercial News

Financial Speculation Recovering; Gold Standard Money Initially Weak then Firm; Swap Rate Drops to 7.5 Yuan Before Rebounding Strongly by 1.9 Yuan 142

The gold market was initially weak yesterday before exhibiting hidden strength. Major players had differing demands for supply, while retail investors initially exited before re-entering. Favorable rumors spread, and the swap premium actually fell to 7.5 yuan, which boosted confidence. The result was a rebound, and the situation also turned stable. In the early morning, overseas silver markets in both England and the United States were flat. The forward silver price in Montreal fell by 0.5 hao and rose by 0.2 li respectively. Exchange rates slightly narrowed. The price of raw gold in London rose by 1.5 pence. The Central Bank's standard gold bullion price was announced, with both English and American prices flat. The customs gold unit remained unchanged. The listed price of standard gold bullion rose to 1146.9 yuan. People's sentiment stabilized. Off-market provisional trading opened at around 43 yuan. Fuxing, Yonghui, and Xiang made progressive additions, trending upwards. However, due to Hengchang and Yongshang selling and then covering, the morning opening was slightly higher, and it continued to rise after opening. However, because major players took advantage of the high prices to sell, and short sellers also increased their positions, prices gradually declined. Retail investors took the opportunity to sell and turned weak. The HSBC's listed price was announced, with English prices flat and American prices narrowing by 0.0625. Although there was a slight struggle in the middle, prices still fell to 40.06 yuan at one point. However, buyers took advantage of the low prices to maintain them, gradually pulling them up. Since the silver balance tax was announced as unchanged, the situation turned stable, and there was more buying. Later, the foreign firms still had settlement funds, and major players purchased. After that, the market lacked supply and gradually prospered. Although predictions for Indian silver were one anna higher, the speculation could not wait and rushed to cover. As a result, the buying spree suddenly intensified. At noon, the situation became stable. This was the reaction that was expected after the increase in capital and the reduction of residual positions. However, the trend did not deviate from mediocrity. The future will depend on whether the major players revive their spirits and whether there are stimulating messages from the outside world. The swap premium yesterday was only 7.5 yuan for short sellers. The capital for the January period has increased to more than 12,800 units. The market situation for the first half of the day is recorded below.

The morning opening was 1143.3 yuan, 0.8 yuan better than the previous close. Huixiang, Tongyu, Runmao, and Hengyu made progressive additions, rising to 4.2 yuan. Dadecheng, Richang, Houyu, Tongtaichang, Yuqingyong, and Chunyuanyong sold in succession, falling to 0.08 yuan. Yifengyong, Yicheng, and Fuyu took advantage of the low prices to add, rebounding to 2.4 yuan. Dadecheng and Hengyu still sold at high prices, falling back to 1.6 yuan. The announcement of the silver balance tax did not offer any encouragement. The situation was stable, and the foreign firms still had settlement funds. Dafayong and Yuanmaoyong increased to 2.7 yuan. Fuyu and Dadecheng withdrew, falling to 1.4 yuan. Jinfengyong, Dadecheng, Yicheng, Qianyuan Yong, and retail investors all bought, gradually rising to 3 yuan. Predictions for Indian silver were one anna higher. Fuyu, Hengchang, and Yongshang sold and slightly covered. Retail investors Hongkangyong, Fuxingyong, Yifengyong, and Lichang still bought, rising to 4.4 yuan. Dadecheng and Richang still sold at 3.8 yuan. Tongfu, Qianchangxiang, Hongkangyong, and Richang re-entered to 4.8 yuan. The closing price was 1144.4 yuan. The market at the close was still stable.

The settlement price, based on the Central Bank's standard gold bullion price, was listed at 1146.9 yuan, approximately 2 yuan higher than the closing price, and 1 yuan weaker than the previous close. Dried Goods: Orchid Bamboo Branches are in Short Supply, Prices Rise by 2-3 Yuan 159

The output of orchid bamboo branches produced in Zhangzhou this year is inherently small. Previously, due to sluggish sales in Shanghai, most of the goods here were diverted to Wenzhou for sale, resulting in extremely thin inventories and few stocks on hand. Lately, there have been no new arrivals, and with active sales in Zhejiang, there is a sudden feeling of supply not meeting demand, and a great sense of shortage. Yesterday, the market price had already rebounded by 2-3 yuan, and the market trend was brisk.

Oil Market: Cottonseed Crude Oil Exports Suddenly Improve 160

Due to the lack of sales in Shanghai and by out-of-town brokers, cottonseed refined oil has long been in a weak market. However, crude oil, which few people pay attention to, has seen a sudden surge in overseas sales markets this week. Various oil pressing factories in Shanghai have been selling off, with a large volume of up to 300 tons traded. The price was uniformly 17 yuan, stipulated to be per 100 jin on the Sima scale, with taxes and fees to be added. Jardine Matheson, Jardine Engineering Corporation, and Bao Long Foreign Firm, among others, were buying for delivery in December and January. The market prices they set were all based on verbal agreements, it is said.

Silk and Tea: Needle, Xiuxian, and Mei Green Teas Sell Sparsely 161

Yesterday, the green tea market situation remained lackluster. Sales of high-grade Zhenmei from Wuyuan and Tunxi, among other places, have not yet started. Stocks of Gongxi and Gongzhu teas, as well as Baitu Zhuang, are also taking a wait-and-see approach. However, the Moroccan market still has sparse sales of needle and xiuxian teas. Yesterday, Jardine Matheson, China Yongxing, and other firms continued to buy in more than 200 boxes, with no change in selling prices.

Piece Goods: Long-Pile Silk Camel Down Sells Briskly in a Timely Manner 162

New long-pile silk woven camel down is particularly popular this year because long coats for men and women are extremely fashionable, and most people with some assets are having them made. Because, apart from clothing shops that process the goods, the wool merchants on Qipan Street do not make custom orders, there are not many arrivals, and supply cannot meet demand. Top-grade goods are mostly sold for 22-23 yuan, and second-grade goods are sold for 15-16 yuan. Inventories are still scarce, and the market sentiment is more favorable than that of top-grade goods. Most of those who have inventory are unwilling to compromise, and both wholesale and retail sales must be paid in cash, which is truly rare recently. Upon investigation, this type of new long-pile camel down men's and women's coats actually cannot keep out the cold. As soon as they encounter rain or snow, the pile is ruined. Therefore, it is only welcomed by the propertied class in this corner of the sea who emphasize fashion and boast of beauty. There is no other way out, so it is predicted that its time in the limelight will not last long.

Hardware: Dongbai Iron Price Drops Frequently 163

Transactions in Dongbai iron have been very sluggish recently. Because out-of-town brokers have stopped buying, and factory sales are also sluggish, the market situation is very weak. Therefore, the industry is hesitant to place orders with Osaka, and there has been no news of transactions for a month. However, a telegram arrived from Osaka yesterday stating that the price of 3' x 7' Dongbai iron has fallen from 1 yuan (Japanese yen) to 88 fen (Japanese yen) per sheet. It is said that the local industry has not placed orders due to lack of profit. It is expected that the market will inevitably see further declines.

Spring and Autumn Children's Weekly

Save the Children 164

— Yangzijiang

People say: "Save the middle school students." I say: We should even more "Save the Children"!

Look at the adults in China. They are either timid as mice or accustomed to complacency, not striving for improvement. Westerners like to explore, like to fly into the stratosphere in hot air balloons, but in China, we don't hear about this kind of scientific exploration. If there is any, they are just acting as guides or assistants for Westerners in places like Tibet. How did things get to this point? My answer is: as children, they were made timid by parents who didn't understand educational principles.

This fact hasn't changed even now, that parents (mostly mothers), in order to coax small children to sleep, always say: "Listen! The jackal is coming, the tiger is coming, good baby. Go to sleep quickly!" At the same time, parents or other people imitate the roar of a wolf or tiger in the dark. "Once frightened, the child falls asleep," especially when the child is crying, this method is used the most.

Once or twice is not a big deal, but over time, it will have a serious impact on the child's psychology. In tangible terms: adults' fear of walking at night, fear of entering remote mountains, that kind of wary and cowardly attitude, was undoubtedly nurtured when they were children. In intangible terms: the whole nation's hesitancy, lack of a firm fighting stance, is probably related to childhood education, isn't it?

Now that the National Children's Year Binxie Committee has just opened, I would like to raise this subtle but also quite important issue to urge educators and parents to pay attention.

A Few Clever Children in History 165

— Wang Min

Little friends: Do you like to know more stories about clever children in history, like Sima Guang smashing the jar to save the drowning child, and Wen Yanbo filling the jar with water to retrieve the ball? Here, let me introduce a few more.

During the Later Han Dynasty, Huang Wan's grandfather, named Qiong, was the prefect of Wei Commandery. One year, during a solar eclipse, the Empress Dowager asked Huang Qiong: "How much was eclipsed?" Huang Qiong didn't know the shape of the solar eclipse, so he couldn't answer for a moment. Huang Wan was only seven years old at the time, but he said to Huang Qiong: "Just say that the remaining sun is almost the same as the crescent moon, and that will be correct." Huang Qiong followed his words and reported it, and the Empress Dowager praised him greatly.

Yang Xiu was only nine years old when Kong Rong visited his home. His father brought out bayberries, and Kong Rong said to him, "These are your family's fruits." He replied to Kong Rong, "I haven't heard that peacocks are your family's birds."

Xu Xuan, the prime minister of the Southern Tang Dynasty's Li Houzhu, was already able to write articles when he was ten years old. One day, he was writing a poem about the sounds of autumn, and he finished it in no time. Li He and Pei Jing of the Tang Dynasty were also able to write articles at the age of seven.

During the Jin Dynasty, Wang Rong, at the age of six or seven, was playing games with children by the roadside. He saw that the plums on the plum tree bore a lot of fruit, and the children all went to pick and eat them, but Wang Rong didn't pick them alone. Someone asked him, "Why don't you like to pick and eat them?" He said, "The tree bears so much fruit by the roadside, they must be bitter plums." The children who picked the plums tasted them and found that they were indeed bitter.

During the Han Dynasty, Zhang Tang's father was the administrator of Chang'an when Zhang Tang was young. One day, his father went out and told Zhang Tang to guard the house. A piece of meat was stolen by a rat, and his father suspected that he had eaten it, so he beat him. Later, he dug the hole, caught the rat, and found the remaining meat stolen by the rat. He then sat in court alone and sentenced the rat as a prisoner. All the arrangements were very much like an old official.

Sea Creatures 166

— Rong

One morning, Xiao Ming was sitting alone at the table eating breakfast. On the table were jellyfish, fried dough sticks, meat floss, etc. He thought the jellyfish tasted good and was crispy, but he didn't understand what it was. After finishing his porridge, he went to ask his older brother, Xiao Cong: "Brother Cong, what is the name of the side dish in the small bowl that I ate with my porridge just now?" Xiao Cong thought for a moment and said: "Oh, that's called jellyfish. It's produced in the southeastern coastal areas of our country. It can be divided into two parts, the upper part is a flat, round, and wide fleshy film, the color is white, the surface is very smooth, and the center is raised into an umbrella shape. The texture is loose and crispy. This is called the umbrella part. The lower part is called the stalk, which is thick and long, and has two-sided forked flesh. The jellyfish you ate for breakfast was its skin, called jellyfish skin. There are many other kinds of things produced in the sea. Now I'll tell you about a few:

1. Stonehead Fish: Also called yellow croaker, because its head is as hard as a stone, so it is called stonehead. Its teeth are sharp, thin, and hard, its mouth is in front of its head, and it has a swim bladder in its belly. The bladder can expand and contract. When it contracts, the body sinks; when it expands, the body floats. Its fins are slightly similar to those of carp, but its tail fin is not forked, like a circle. It has an anal fin, pectoral fin, pelvic fin, dorsal fin, and caudal fin. The anal fin and dorsal fin keep the body stable, the pectoral fin and pelvic fin are used for paddling forward, and the caudal fin is of course used for turning. Its meat is very delicious and can be dried.

2. Sea Cucumber: Its body is similar to a cylinder, and the flesh is soft and thick. Its mouth is at the front of its body, and its back has many uneven nodules. Its meat can also be eaten, and it has many small pieces around its mouth, called tentacles, which are used for predation. It can also be dried and sold to various places. In the hot pot we eat during the New Year, there is a dark brown thing, which is dried sea cucumber.

3. Coral: It lives in warm seas and its body is constantly swaying. When it encounters aquatic animals that are smaller than it, it uses the eight pairs of small tentacles around its mouth to prey on them. Its structure is extremely simple, with only one sac, which is its body cavity and gastrointestinal tract, so it is called a coelenterate. What we usually see is a coral tree, which is the skeleton of coral polyps. It can be made into various rings, buttons, hairpins, etc. as decorations, which are very beautiful. There are red, white, and agate colors, and the price is not expensive, and the production is also very high.

Winter Has Arrived 167

— Cheng Ming

Winter has arrived, the north wind roars like a tiger's howl, the weather is terribly cold. I wear a cotton robe on my body, and wool gloves on my hands. I wear an aviator hat on my head, and the children's happiness is truly like this.

Winter has arrived, I get up early in the morning and eat my fill, I carry my schoolbag to school. The teacher teaches us to do morning exercises, to strengthen our bodies and spirits, and the cold air is completely dispelled by the exercises.

Winter has arrived, the disaster area refugees are miserable, they have no clothes to wear, and no food to eat. Hunger and cold are intertwined, and their lives cannot be protected. I advise the children to save on sweets and miscellaneous expenses to help these suffering compatriots.

Children's Corner

Min'er's Suffering 168

— Liu Guoying, 6th Grade, West Xia Elementary School

Min'er is a child from a farming family. His family was originally a very happy family, and his parents loved him very much. But when he was nine years old, his mother died. Since his mother died, he has felt very unhappy and often sad and tearful. Soon his father married a stepmother, who was very hateful. One day, when his father was out, his stepmother often beat or scolded him, and often asked him to do difficult things. Min'er was very young, so he didn't know how to do them, so his stepmother beat him severely. He thought of his own mother's love, so he went to his mother's grave and cried for a long time. When he returned home, it was already late. His stepmother beat him so badly that his skin was broken and he couldn't move. Later, a very loyal old servant carried him to bed and asked a doctor to treat him. Although his injuries were healed, he was treated like a slave by his stepmother every day. When his father returned, he learned of these things and drove his stepmother out. From then on, his father never remarried.

The Pitiful Children 169

— Ba Ling

Going to a familiar bathhouse to bathe, I felt something was different.

Looking closely, ah! Everything was as usual, there was no change. However, the clerk who greeted the guests had changed from an adult to a child.

I was very curious and also very heartbroken! So, after bathing, I started talking to a little clerk.

He said: "I am only fifteen years old this year. I am from Yangzhou. When I was young, I studied for three or four years, but later because of family difficulties, I stopped studying. I helped my parents farm in the fields, but it is difficult to farm in the countryside now! The harvest is not good, so they introduced me to do this kind of work. I have only been in Shanghai for a short time, only half a month!" After speaking, he ran off to greet other guests, making tea, wringing towels, massaging feet... and so on.

After hearing the little clerk's words, I couldn't help but remain silent for a long time. I thought: Isn't this year Children's Year? The mission of Children's Year is to seek happiness for general children. Now, where is the happiness of children? Children who should be educated, but have not had the opportunity to be educated, is this the happiness of children? For such a child to be able to scrape together a living in a bathhouse is considered great luck. But there are still hundreds of thousands of children wandering the streets, suffering from hunger and cold, with no fixed place to live. What a serious problem this is!

Save the children? Pay attention to the happiness of children, gentlemen!

Why Does Oil Float on the Surface of Water? 170

— Shi

Little friends, have you seen oil on the surface of water? Oil is a liquid, so why can it float on top of another liquid? Isn't this a very strange thing? No, it's not strange! As long as we observe carefully, we will understand.

Generally speaking, if we want to know whether something can float on the surface of water, the first condition is that we have to see whether this thing will dissolve in water. For example, if we take a piece of salt and put it in water, it will immediately disappear. This is the result of dissolution. The properties of oil are different from this. Not only does it not dissolve in water, but also the same volume of water is much lighter, so it can float on the surface of water.

Little friends, do you understand this small problem?

A Book on Children's Science Lectures 172

— Lin Yin

(3) How Books are Printed

Little friends may want to ask me, how are the pictures in books printed?

Yes, this is a question worth exploring. The illustrations in books are sometimes printed using zinc plates, sometimes copper plates, and sometimes lithography.

Zinc and copper plates are usually attached to lead plates cast with lead type for printing. The method of making a zinc plate is to first photograph the original artwork onto a wet plate using a camera, then print it onto a clean zinc plate. The unwanted parts are then eaten away with chemicals, resulting in the finished plate. The method of making a copper plate is similar to that of making a zinc plate, except that a screen is added during photography. This screen is composed of small dots of varying sizes. The artwork with the screen is then printed onto a steel plate.

The above only applies to printing in a single color, which is commonly referred to as monochrome printing. To print beautiful colors, lithography is used. The process of lithography involves first separating the original artwork into several colors, tracing the lines with lithographic ink, one sheet for each color, and placing it onto a smooth stone slab that has been coated with chemicals. (Picture 4) The areas on the stone slab without ink will not absorb ink because they have been treated with chemicals, while the areas drawn with lithographic ink will absorb ink, allowing for the desired printing. Each color requires this process to be repeated. Therefore, the cost is much higher. Beautiful color pictures in ordinary books, as well as market paintings and calendars, are printed using this method.

In recent years, printing technology has become even more advanced, with the invention of collotype and photogravure, which can produce prints that are identical to the originals and do not fade, which is a great boon to the cultural world!

The artwork in (Picture 1) is printed using a zinc plate, while the artwork in (Picture 2) is printed using a copper plate. (Picture 3) shows an enlarged view of the screen.

The Story of the White Mountain Crow (10) (2) 173

— Xi

How uncomfortable it is for a bachelor to live in such an inn! I want to find my own kind and ask them to take me in. But I thought, "At night, all crows are gray, and it's impossible to tell which one is my own kind. Besides, it might be inconvenient to live next to them?"

First, I flew towards a ditch, where I saw many European rollers gathered. They were carefully doing their evening grooming. I saw that they all had golden wings and shiny claws—how beautiful! They were the dandies of the forest. They were very kind, but they didn't pay attention to me. All they talked about was empty and meaningless: some talked about their quarrels with people, and others talked about their pursuit of the opposite sex. They looked conceited, which I couldn't stand, so I couldn't stay here any longer.

"Then I perched on a branch and saw five or six different kinds of birds lined up there. I humbly stayed on the tip of the branch, hoping they would allow me to spend the night here. Unfortunately, the one next to me was an old turtledove, as dry as a weathervane on a roof. When I got close to her, she pretended to be tidying her sparse feathers, as if she was afraid of pulling one out. I accidentally touched her with the tip of my wing, and she straightened up proudly, puffed out her beak, and said, "Sir, what do you mean?" Then she elbowed me hard, knocking me down.

I fell into a pile of bushes and saw a fat female bunting sleeping peacefully. My mother was fat, but not as plump as she was. I secretly crawled next to her, saying to myself, "She certainly won't wake up. Even if she does, a good fat mother like her probably won't be angry with me." But the reality was not like that. She half-opened her eyes and sighed slightly, "Child, you're disturbing me! Get out of here quickly!"

At the same time, I heard someone calling me: it turned out that some thrushes were calling me to come over from the top of a rowan tree. I thought to myself, "I've finally met some good friends here. They raised their seats to let me stay, laughing like crazy!" I flapped my wings and flew straight into their midst. But before long, I saw that these ladies had eaten too many grapes, and their bellies were so swollen that they could hardly support the branches. Their dull jokes, crazy laughter, and frivolous songs all made me have to fly away.

I began to despair and decided to sleep in a quiet corner. At this moment, a nightingale began to sing. Everyone was silent. Oh! How clear his voice was, and how sweet it felt in his melancholy! His singing not only didn't disturb people's sleep, but it was like a lullaby that made people fall asleep peacefully. No one tried to stop him, and no one complained about him singing in the middle of the night; his father would never scold him, and his friends would never fly away when they heard his singing.
